Young Siamese Military Officers Go to Japan for Training

(Tokyo) The first group of ten young Siamese military officers coming to Japan for training arrived in Kobe today aboard a Japanese ship from Bangkok. They are expected to arrive in Tokyo tomorrow. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

Japan Eager to Promote Japan-Siam Amity Plan

World News Agency, Tokyo: Siam's pro-Japanese tendencies have always been very strong. At the League of Nations General Assembly two years ago, the Manchurian issue was debated, and Japan's claims were denied by a vote of 42 to 1. At that time, only the Siamese representative abstained, indicating goodwill towards Japan. Also, since the current government of Arpa Hongsa was established in June of the same year after a revolution in that country, the relationship between Japan and Siam has rapidly progressed. Last year, the current Siamese ambassador to Japan, Mitrakan Kamraksa, has been eagerly promoting Japan-Siam friendship. Furthermore, Yasuke Yatabe, the Japanese ambassador to Siam, who has been in office for six years, has also gained the trust of the Siamese government and plays an important role in the concretization of the two countries' friendship. Last year, the Siamese government recruited cotton cultivation technicians and lecturers specializing in agricultural economics from Japan, and also decided to send naval officers and cadets from their country to engage in ocean voyages on Japanese ships. As for this year's plans, Siam intends to send a dance troupe to Japan to introduce Siamese art, and also plans to establish a guidance organization for international students to increase the number of Japanese students studying abroad, and further import Japanese medical technology. On the Japanese side, in order to promote political reform in Siam, it will spare no effort to provide all possible assistance. It also plans to establish a new hygiene and medical technology organization aimed at the Siamese public. In the naval field, it is conducting a long-distance flight plan to visit Bangkok. The government is also considering establishing a new air route between Bangkok and Japan. All parties have great expectations for the progress of Japan-Siam friendship this year.

US and Japan Compete to Open Aviation Routes

Los Angeles: According to reliable sources received here, trans-Pacific airmail service may begin in April this year. Mr. Li, the Pacific Coast manager of the Ma Zhen Shipping Company, declined to comment on this news, but said that the date is approaching. (National Telegram, 17th)

(Washington) Air links between the United States and Europe will soon be realized. President Roosevelt will request Congress to allocate funds to build a Zeppelin-style airship within the next week, so that two regular air routes can be opened simultaneously this summer, one flying between the American Pacific coast and Honolulu, Hawaii, and the other flying between Europe and America via the Bermuda and Azores islands in the Atlantic Ocean. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

(Tokyo) The problem of developing air routes between Tokyo and Changchun, and between Tokyo and the South Seas, through a joint Japanese-Manchurian venture using Zeppelin airships, initiated by Peer Kabayama Sukehide, Baron Izuto Kiyoshi, former director of the East Asia Development Bureau Ozaki Keiichi, and Doctor of Law Honda Kumato, has recently been progressing rapidly. The airport has been internally designated to be located on a hundred thousand or more tsubo of land in Mobara, Chiba Prefecture. The company name has also been decided to be Pacific Aviation Co., Ltd., and a preparation office has been established, which will be established in mid-March. It will order airships from Zeppelin Company, with a capital of 30 million yen. First, air routes between Tokyo and Changchun, and between Tokyo and the Dutch East Indies will be established. In the future, it also plans to open air routes between Australia, Tokyo, and the United States. It will first use 10 million yen to order an airship from the German Zeppelin Company that is more than one and a half times larger than the Zeppelin airship. In the future, it also plans to build two or three ships by itself. (Electric Communication Dispatch, 17th)

British Strengthen Air Defense

Airfield Built Northwest of London

Expansion of Isle of Wight Base

(London) The Aviation Department is about to build three new military airfields northwest of London. Once completed, the British air defense line, which runs parallel to the coast, will be completed, and the British public's demand for air defense can be said to be satisfied. In addition to building airfields, the air defense plan proposed by the Aviation Department also involves reorganizing the British central defense works and planning to conduct surveys on the southern coast to select sites for aerial bombing practice ranges. The aviation base on the Isle of Wight is also planned to be expanded. (Note: The Isle of Wight is located in southern England, directly in front of the Portsmouth naval base, and its strategic position is extremely important.) (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Page 10

Saar Region Returns to Germany - League of Nations Council Unanimously Approves

Formal Handover on March 1st - Franco-German Agreement Greatly Reassures People

All Outstanding Issues to be Resolved Within One Month

(Geneva) The Council of the League of Nations unanimously approved at 9 p.m. tonight the return of the Saar to Germany on March 1st, based on the recommendation of the Saar Committee of Three. Although the passage of this motion was widely anticipated, its rapid resolution relieved the tense emotions of the world. Prior to the meeting, representatives from Germany and France fully agreed before the Italian representative, Mr. Aloisi, on the demilitarization of the Saar region. The Council of the League of Nations convened a meeting at around 8 p.m.

Mr. Aloisi's Report

Mr. Aloisi was the first to stand and report that the people of the Saar, in all electoral districts, had overwhelmingly expressed their desire to be reunited with Germany. Therefore, the Committee of Three, based on the will of the people, proposed the following recommendations: (1) The entire Saar region should be incorporated into Germany, in accordance with Article 48 of the Treaty of Versailles and the clauses related to the plebiscite; (2) It is stipulated that Germany will restore sovereignty over the Saar region on March 1st; (3) The Saar Committee, together with the governments of Germany and France and the Saar Governing Commission, will determine all necessary preparations for the change of government and the procedures for fulfilling various obligations. If these preparations are not agreed upon by February 15th, the Committee of Three should submit a recommendation to the Council of the League of Nations, so that the Council can directly handle the matter in accordance with the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles and the various clauses of the plebiscite events recognized by both Germany and France.

French Foreign Minister's Speech

After Mr. Aloisi's report, French Foreign Minister Laval stood up and stated the French government's intentions, saying that the results of the Saar plebiscite were very clear and there was no doubt about the will of the people. Therefore, the fate of the Saar's future has been freely decided by its people. Under these circumstances, the Council of the League of Nations can only decide to incorporate the Saar into Germany. France had anticipated the Council's decision in advance. However, France has always firmly believed in the principle that treaties are sacred and inviolable.

The League of Nations' Mission is Not Over Yet. Now the League of Nations has repeatedly demonstrated its efforts to achieve peace in this difficult situation, which is truly admirable. However, the League of Nations' mission cannot be said to be over yet. Before the Saar region merges with Germany, many important issues remain to be resolved. The League of Nations Committee has a difficult task ahead, and the committee should consult with the governments of both countries and the Saar Governing Commission to establish the conditions for the transfer of sovereignty and prepare various methods for abolishing the current government of the Saar. There are many and complex problems to be resolved. However, the results already achieved will promote the final solution.

Do Not Leave Any Traces of Animosity. Laval continued, saying that the German leader had addressed the people of the Saar yesterday, saying that they should strictly maintain order so that the return of the Saar to Germany would not leave any blemishes in history. Hitler's remarks indicated that after the plebiscite, there would be no more animosity or retaliation towards the people who exercised their free will in accordance with the privileges granted by the terms. Because the final solution must not leave any traces of animosity, and the people of the world hope that it can be carried out with a solemn attitude.

Accepting Immigrants is Humane. The reason why France cannot close its borders is purely out of humanitarian considerations. If problems arise regarding the Saar immigration issue in the future, the League of Nations should handle it fairly.

Accept Hitler's Promise. Laval went on to say that the German leader Hitler had repeatedly expressed his desire for peace in welcoming the return of the Saar, and said that there would be no further territorial disputes with France. I now accept this statement, and in fact, the harmony between France and Germany is the most important condition for European peace. France is a country that loves peace, but based on the lessons learned from history, France should also have adequate guarantees, and other countries naturally have the same rights. Therefore, when international treaties are concluded to mutually guarantee each other, we should not hesitate to join cooperation.

Speeches by British and Russian Representatives

After Laval's speech, British Lord Privy Seal Eden and Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov stood up one after another and made speeches, saying that the satisfactory resolution of the Saar issue proved the honor of both countries and the League of Nations' position. The Council of the League of Nations then unanimously approved the recommendation of the Committee of Three, and then the chairman, Mr. Ruyshdi, stood up to give a thank-you speech and announced the adjournment of the meeting. (National Telegram, 17th)

(Geneva) France and Italy reached an agreement on the handover of the Saar, and it was decided that it would be managed by Germany on March 1st. This agreement was subsequently approved by the Council of the League of Nations, and the people's hearts were greatly relieved. The agreement stated that Articles 41 and 42 of the Treaty of Versailles concerning the demilitarization of the Rhineland would be applied to the Saar. If existing financial problems, such as the rights of officials and social insurance, are not resolved, the Council of the League of Nations will convene on February 15 to receive them and seek solutions. British representative Eden spoke at the Council meeting to welcome the agreement, saying that he hoped that the passage of this agreement would help international understanding. This agreement respects both parties and the League of Nations. French Foreign Minister Laval stated that France had already accepted the results of the citizens' assembly vote. He believed in Hitler's words that no disreputable connections should be made to the return of the Saar, meaning that there should be no retaliatory actions. For humanitarian reasons, France does not refuse to accept Saar refugees, but these refugees will become an international problem, and France intends to raise this matter to the Council. Hitler said on January 13 that he had taken firm steps towards Franco-German friendship. It is important to know that no government today can refuse to participate in the establishment of a convention aimed at enabling signatory countries to obtain the mutual guarantees they need. In his final words, Mr. Lai said, "We should strive to make good use of the recent agreement established in Rome." (Reuters)

Outline of Franco-German Agreement

(Geneva) The Saar Committee of Three, after a long period of discussion and telephone contact with Berlin, has now reached an agreement between France and Germany on the Saar issue. The outline is as follows:

(1) The Council of the League of Nations shall decide on the reunification of the Saar region with Germany in accordance with the conditions arising from the Treaty of Versailles. Therefore, the clauses on the abolition of armaments in the Treaty of Versailles shall also apply uniformly in the Saar region.

(2) It is stipulated that Germany shall recover the territory of the Saar region from March 1st of this year.

(3) All outstanding issues related to the Saar region, including business negotiations held in Berlin and Paris, shall be completely resolved before February 15th, and the League of Nations shall file them based on the report of the Saar Committee of Three. If all outstanding issues have not been completely resolved by February 15th, the Committee of Three shall submit a recommendation to the Council, and the Council shall convene a special meeting to take necessary decisions.

This compromise on the Saar issue has been delayed for a long time, and the main difficulties are two: one is the issue of demilitarization of the Saar region, and the other is the arbitration power of the Council of the League of Nations on issues related to French interests. Germany advocated restricting the scope of the Council's decision-making power, limiting it only to the establishment of a new political system in the Saar, while France demanded that the Council have the power to clear up all past outstanding issues, such as private debt issues. The first of these two difficulties, such as issues related to the police and the establishment of airfields, has been agreed upon in principle, and the second is now also agreed upon. Therefore, in tonight's Council meeting, there should be no more difficulties, and the resolution on the Saar issue can be safely passed. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

Hitler's Declaration: Germany is Willing to Work for Peace

Reiterates That There Will Be No Future Territorial Disputes with France

Equality is the Only Condition for Returning to the League of Nations

(London) German leader Hitler, in a conversation with London Daily Mail correspondent Price today, made a firm statement on Germany's commitment to peace. The conversation took place in Munich. Hitler's statement included the following points: First, Germany itself will never disrupt peace; second, if others invade Germany, it would be like walking into a trap, saying, "We have now voluntarily assured France that after the Saar issue is resolved, we will have no other territorial disputes. At the same time, I dare to say that we will never sacrifice our equal rights in the international community under duress." Mr. Shan asked under what conditions Germany could return to the League of Nations. Hitler's answer was quite indignant, saying, "No one in Germany is willing to make returning to the League of Nations contingent on any conditions. There is only one thing to be resolved: whether Germany can participate again with full equality." Hitler also stated that Germany has absolutely no intention of challenging for its own benefit, and said, "If the interests of other countries have nothing to do with Germany, we are even less willing to resort to force on their behalf." (National Telegram, 18th)

Franco-German Negotiations Scheduled for Saar Aftermath

To Be Held in Berlin Next Monday

(Paris) Negotiations between France and Germany on the aftermath of the Saar plebiscite will begin in Berlin on the 21st of this month. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

The Political Status of the Third Germany is Consolidated

No Statement on Austria

Italian Newspapers Deeply Disappointed

(Rome) Since the victory of the Saar plebiscite, the political status of the Third Germany has been consolidated. However, the German government has neither made a formal declaration nor issued a comment, providing a definite guarantee that Germany, having won the Saar vote, will not have any further ambitions for other parts of Europe in the future, especially for Austria. There has also been no indication regarding the possibility of Germany returning to the League of Nations. Therefore, Italian newspapers are quite disappointed. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

Refugees Flee in Disarray

Saarbrücken. Early this morning, a Reuters reporter at the Saar station in Beringen witnessed 500 men, women, and children fleeing from the Saar, staggering out of the station in a state of disarray. Most of these people were Germans and opponents of Hitlerism. Having heard that the Saar Governing Commission had issued a warning that if they remained in the territory, their safety could not be guaranteed, they moved in haste. After the local government provided them with a meal, they were transported by train to Toulouse. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

Saarbrücken. Today, touring the Saar border and the French province of Lorraine, I saw that the number of people fleeing from the Saar into French territory is increasing daily, including people of all levels, and Jews are not a few. There are now more than 400 people passing through Saarguemines, and another hundred passing through Forbach. The French patrol team on the border is now strictly guarded, allowing only those with French passports to enter. Those who are allowed in are provided with food and lodging by the French authorities, but the expenses will be collected from the League of Nations. Although several refugees mentioned the brutality of the National Socialist Party, a special Reuters reporter was unable to find anyone who had been insulted. Leaders of the German Front claimed that the fears of the Communists, Socialists, and Jews regarding atrocities were unfounded. However, the refugees still believe that the current calm is the tranquility before the storm, and that an outbreak of opponents of Hitler in the Saar is imminent. For several days, crowds have gathered in front of the Saar French consulate to wait to receive passports to go abroad, which is sufficient evidence of the general panic of the people. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

(Paris) Saar region Socialist leader Blum, who was one of the strongest advocates of maintaining the status quo, fled to France for safety after the Saar vote decided to return to Germany. According to reports, Mr. Blum will give a speech at a meeting somewhere, advocating that various fascist groups should be dissolved. A member of the Paris City Council, upon hearing this, immediately requested the Chief of Police to notify Mr. Blum that he was being accommodated in France and should behave with courtesy and not make such remarks. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

Laval Returns to Paris Tonight to Plan the Completion of the Eastern European Pact

(Paris) According to reliable sources, French Foreign Minister Laval will depart from Geneva tomorrow night and arrive in Paris on Sunday. In the next two days, he will consult with representatives from Britain, Italy, Russia, the Little Entente, Hungary, and Turkey to complete the Eastern European Locarno Pact. (National Telegram, 18th)

(Geneva) Representatives from various countries continued to hold talks outside the Council of the League of Nations. This conference was originally scheduled to be held yesterday, but was postponed to this afternoon due to the Council's discussion of the Saar issue. At lunchtime, Mr. Lai had lunch with Austrian Foreign Minister Weidigger. After the meal, he met with Spanish representative Madariaga. It is generally believed that the work of the Council will come to an end, and Laval can leave for home tomorrow night. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Iran-Iraq Dispute to be Discussed by League of Nations Today

The Situation is Favorable to Persia

(Geneva) The Council of the League of Nations is scheduled to hold a public meeting tomorrow to discuss the dispute between Iraq and Iran (the new name for Persia) over the border issue. Hungary's Reply to the League of Nations

Officials Neglecting Their Duties Have Been Dismissed

Not Responsible for the Marseille Incident

(Geneva) Regarding the demands made by the Council of the League of Nations to Hungary in connection with the assassination of King Alexander of Yugoslavia and French Foreign Minister Barthou in Marseille last October, the Hungarian government's reply today stated that the Hungarian government has implemented them, punishing the responsible officials. The document also firmly stated that it cannot be definitively proven that the Hungarian authorities had a direct or indirect relationship with the Marseille massacre. The Hungarian government has now tightened passport regulations and strictly manages foreigners. It is reported that the officials who have been punished are two police chiefs who have been dismissed, a commander of the Gendarmerie who has been detained for 30 days, and two Gendarmerie officers who have received short prison sentences. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

MacDonald's Speech Emphasizes Stabilizing International Exchange Rates

Otherwise, Other Issues Cannot Be Resolved

The International Situation is Becoming Clearer, Britain is a Powerful Force

Rumors of Early Re-Election of Parliament Are Untrue

Newcastle. Prime Minister MacDonald, in a speech here today, emphasized the need to stabilize international exchange rates as soon as possible, saying that if we cannot solve the international exchange rate issue, we will never be able to satisfactorily solve other issues, because the international exchange rate issue is encountered every day. Recently, the US dollar has fluctuated, and there have been rumors that the United States will restore the gold standard. It is said that the stability of the US dollar and the gold pound is imminent. It is particularly noteworthy that the Prime Minister delivered this speech at this time. (National Telegram, 17th)

(London) Prime Minister MacDonald recently delivered a speech at the Rotary Club of Newcastle, defending the methods and undertakings adopted by the current cabinet, saying that the cabinet's domestic and foreign affairs will achieve complete victory when the international situation becomes clearer, the will for European peace is promoted, and national mutual trust is promoted. The British cabinet is a powerful factor. Regarding the economic aspect, the tariff protection policy should not be rigidly adhered to, but should adhere to the principles of sound economics. Over-intervention by the state is inevitable and inappropriate. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

(London) Recently, the Labor Party has repeatedly spread rumors that the general election of Parliament will be held within this year, and there have been such rumors abroad. Prime Minister MacDonald recently declared, "There are rumors abroad that the government intends to hold the general election of Parliament early for some reason. In fact, these rumors are entirely fabricated. I am the head of the government, so I would like to make the truth known to people at home and abroad. Our acquisition of power is to improve the fate of the people. We must use every minute of our time to gradually achieve our goals." (Vasi dispatch, 16th)

French General Weygand Retires

The Positions of Marshal and Chief of Staff of the Army are Merged

(Paris) French General Weygand will turn 68 next Sunday and will retire from his position as Marshal on that day. Army Chief of Staff General Gamelin will succeed him, and it has been decided to merge the positions of Marshal and Army Chief of Staff into one. General Weygand assisted General Foch in handling military affairs during the European War and made great contributions. (Reuters dispatch, 18th)

Soviet Aircraft Conducts Long-Distance Trial Flights in the Far East

In the Lower Reaches of the Heilongjiang River Region

Khabarovsk. Soviet LI-20 aircraft has made a long-distance winter flight to the northern regions of the Far East. This trip is the beginning of regular flights in the lower reaches of the Heilongjiang River region in winter. The aircraft took off from Khabarovsk, passed through the Shantar Islands, Chumikan, Nilkon, and Okhotsk, and returned to Khabarovsk. The pilot was aviator Maislok. The aircraft arrived in Nikolaevsk on the 15th of this month, encountering severe frost during the flight, which lasted four hours and fifty-six minutes. (TASS dispatch, 17th)

Japanese Minister of Commerce and Industry Machida Appointed President of the Minseito Party

(Tokyo) Former President of the Minseito Party Wakatsuki Reijiro returned to Tokyo from Ito, Izu this morning. Party executives went to Wakatsuki's private residence to report on the party's current situation and urged him to ask Minister of Commerce and Industry Machida Chuji to take office as president. Wakatsuki visited Machida at 1:30 p.m., and Machida promised to give it deep consideration. Later, Machida decided to take office and visited the party elders Taketomi and Yamamoto at 3 p.m. He visited Wakatsuki at 4:20 p.m. to inform him that he had decided to take office as president. Therefore, the long-unresolved issue of the president of the Minseito Party has also come to an end. It is reported that after Machida decided to take office as president, he would not resign from the position of Minister of Commerce and Industry. (China United Press dispatch, 18th)

Roosevelt's Message to Congress Urges the Enactment of Social Relief Laws

Those Over 65 Receive a Monthly Pension of More Than 20 Yuan

Unemployment Insurance Deduction of 3% of Wages Paid by Employers

(Washington) President Roosevelt sent a message to Congress yesterday, recommending the adoption of a large-scale social welfare program, including unemployment insurance, pensions, relief for impoverished children, and increased subsidies from the federal government, as well as fundraising by local governments to develop public health in various states, counties, and cities. According to the government's proposed method, this social welfare program should be implemented by the state governments, and the federal government should retain financial management rights. After President Roosevelt's proposal was put forward, New York State Democratic Senator Wagner immediately proposed a social security bill, stipulating that a compulsory pension insurance system should be established from January 1, 1937. The insurance premium is collected at 1% of the wage income, with employers and employees each contributing half. After being insured, Americans can receive a monthly pension of US$22.50 per person from the age of 65. In addition, unemployment insurance measures are stipulated, with the insurance premium being 3% of the wage, which is paid by the employer. The expenses for implementing the social welfare program, including those for pension insurance, are US$150 million per year; those for unemployment insurance are US$50 million per year; and those for child relief are US$28 million per year. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt's message to Congress today stated that the report of the Cabinet Economic Security Committee should be formally adopted as a proposal, so that the people of the whole country can have security in the various dangers of life. This is what the president promised in his message at the opening of Congress. The President now urges Congress to enact the Committee's recommendations into law as soon as possible, without further delay, and stated that all recommendations are suitable for the psychology of the American people. The Committee does not want to force people to do things that are difficult, and has carefully considered all the facts. The message also stated that once this plan is launched with government funding, it will be self-sufficient, and all expenses for paying insurance claims will not need to rely on tax revenue. The proposal also includes measures for the government to assist children who are unable to stand on their own feet and local health agencies, but the President said that he does not intend to hold health insurance for the time being. The start-up cost for implementing this plan is US$100 million. The President believes that this number is less than the funds currently required by the country to deal with economic insecurity. (National Telegram, 17th)

Report on the Work of the Soviet Russian People's Commissar Government

All Industries Have Made Progress

No Fear of Japan

(Moscow) Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, Vyacheslav Molotov, reported on the work of the Soviet government at the All-Union Congress of Soviets. Molotov asserted that over the past four years, the national economy and culture have not only developed significantly, but class relations have also undergone major changes, fundamentally transforming the face of the Soviet Union and enabling socialism to dominate the entire national economy.

Industry Molotov elaborated on the progress of Soviet industry, stating that Soviet factories are now capable of manufacturing their own machinery. Heavy industry has fully completed its annual production plan, and the plan to improve quality will also soon be completed. Quality, he noted, has been the weakest point of Soviet machinery in past years.

Agriculture Molotov then discussed agriculture, pointing out that the degree of collectivization in Soviet Russia in October 1934 was 73.2 percent. He stated that this percentage has certainly increased significantly, as the number of individual farmers joining collective farms has been the highest in recent months. For example, in the western provinces, nearly 5,900 farms have joined collective farms in the past three months, 2,400 in the Leningrad province, and 6,500 in Bashkiria. By the end of the Second Five-Year Plan (1937), the collectivization effort will be fully completed. "I believe we would not be greatly mistaken if we said that this work could be completed even earlier." Molotov further stated that the country's animal husbandry has also improved, with an increase in all types of livestock. He detailed the strengthening of collective farms in terms of economics and organization, stating that due to improvements in the work of collective farms, spring sowing in 1934 began earlier than in previous years, and harvesting and grain delivery were both better and faster than in previous years. This year, collective farming in all states and provinces will continue to improve, and the material conditions of collective farmers will also rise. Molotov also cited figures to demonstrate the improvement in the material and cultural life of collective farmers. Education Molotov then discussed the great success of cultural and social work, stating that Soviet Russia is not only implementing compulsory primary education but also wants to raise the level of universal education to secondary education. There are currently 17.2 million students in primary and secondary schools nationwide, compared to only about 6 million before the revolution. The proportion of illiterate adults, which was 35 percent in 1931, is now 8 percent. Investment in municipal economy and housing construction has reached a total of 6.5 billion rubles, with more than 19 million cubic meters of new housing added in various cities.

Culture The success of national republics and provinces in economic and cultural aspects is most significant. The speed of their industrial development is greater than the average speed of the Soviet Union and Soviet Russia. A characteristic of the state and local budgets of Soviet Russia is the substantial increase in expenditures on cultural work. From 1930 to 1934, the state and local budget amounted to an increase of 4,297,700,000 rubles, of which 3,300 million rubles, or approximately 77 percent, was spent on cultural aspects. The state budget of Soviet Russia for 1935 is 1,708,500,000 rubles, and the local budget is 869.3 million rubles, an increase of 27.9 percent compared to 1934. The construction costs for the entire Soviet Union in 1935 will be 21.2 billion rubles, of which approximately 15 billion will be used within Soviet Russia.

International In his conclusion, Molotov discussed the international situation, stating, "During the past period, the strength of the Soviet Union in the international arena has greatly increased. At the same time, various countries recognize that the Soviet Union is an extremely important factor for peace and international relations throughout the world. No major international problems can be resolved without the participation of the Soviet Union. During this period, the working masses of our country have paid extraordinary attention to our eastern border, where the cause of peace has been repeatedly thwarted. The Soviet Union has always used its steadfast policy of peace to resolve various disputes peacefully." Molotov added (at this point, the audience applauded thunderously), "I believe that our eastern neighbors must understand that our resolution of such complex disputes is by no means due to the weakness of the Soviet Union, but rather to the Soviet Union's determined pursuit of peace. The reason why our eastern border is so peaceful and stable is partly due to the fact that the Soviet Union's foreign policy will continue to resolutely strive for peace, as in the past. At the same time, it is also because our country is prepared (and I must emphasize this) to repel attacks from any direction at any time. I believe that this Congress will instruct the government to continue to vigorously pursue a policy of peace in the future, and to use this as the foundation of its foreign policy, striving to establish normal diplomatic relations with all countries and guaranteeing all methods to strengthen our country's national defense capabilities." (TASS dispatch, 17th)

Soviet Russia Sentences Zinoviev to Ten Years of Imprisonment for Counter-Revolutionary Activities

(Moscow) The verdict of the Military Collegium of the Supreme Court of the Soviet Union regarding the case of Zinoviev and Yevdokimov has been announced here.

Main Text The verdict states that according to the court's investigation and based on the defendants' own confessions, it is proven that Zinoviev, as a counter-Soviet faction member, did organize a secret counter-revolutionary group and was led by the so-called "Moscow Center Group." This group remained in existence until their arrest. Its members included Zinoviev, Shalov, Kuklin, Yevdokimov, Gherdik, Bakayev, Kamenev, Fedulov, and Gor-Shinin. The court confirmed that the Leningrad secret counter-revolutionary group, headed by the "Leningrad Center," was also led by the "Moscow Center Group." The members of the Leningrad group have already been executed for the Kirov assassination case. The court also ordered members of the counter-revolutionary group (whose cases must be further investigated) to testify in court. These individuals (Shavalov and Elkovich) provided the court with many facts regarding the secret counter-revolutionary work of the "Moscow Center Group" (especially regarding Zinoviev, Gherdik, Kuklin, and Yevdokimov). They confirmed that the "Moscow Center Group" had repeatedly attempted to collude with other counter-Soviet groups to expand the struggle against the Soviet regime. The court did not obtain any evidence that members of the "Moscow Center Group" had incited the assassination of Kirov. However, the court did confirm that members of the "Moscow Center Group" counter-revolutionary group were aware of the terrorist tendencies of the Leningrad organization, and that they had incited such tendencies. Verdict All defendants confessed to their crimes. The Supreme Court announced the following sentences: Zinoviev, as the main organizer and most active leader of the secret counter-revolutionary group "Moscow Center," was sentenced to ten years of imprisonment. Gherdik, Kuklin, and Shakov, as the most active members of the group, were each sentenced to ten years of imprisonment. Shalov, Yevdokimov, Bakayev, Gor-Shinin, and Chailkov, for actively participating in the work of the group, were each sentenced to eight years of imprisonment. Fedulov, Heilsuburg, Heissen, Tilosov, Panlyemov, Annishev, and Vavilov, for participating in the work of the group, were each sentenced to six years of imprisonment. Kamenev, Bashkirov, and Brav, for participating in the work of the group but not actively, were each sentenced to five years of imprisonment.

The court decided to confiscate all private property of the convicts. The Extraordinary Meeting of the Internal Affairs Commission sentenced 49 members of Zinoviev's counter-revolutionary group to four to five years of imprisonment in detention camps, and 29 people were exiled to various places for two to five years. (TASS dispatch, 17th)

Conclusion of the Jiangxi Highway Bureau Affairs Meeting

(Nanchang) The expanded affairs meeting of the Jiangxi Highway Bureau, lasting three days, concluded on the 18th. A total of more than 240 proposals were submitted and summarized into five categories: (1) promoting social and cultural work, (2) constructing unfinished highways, (3) developing freight transport to promote rural prosperity, (4) increasing revenue and reducing expenditure on materials, and (5) leading rural people to implement new transportation initiatives. The results of the discussions over the past few days have been excellent. (Central News Agency dispatch, 18th)

Fujian Officials and People Cooperate to Dredge Waterways

(Fuzhou) In the provincial capital's suburban and urban waterways, the authorities are conscripting laborers to dredge them. In addition to the military police, civil servants from various agencies are also not exempt. The commencement ceremony was held separately at the Shuibu Men and Jin'an Bridge on the 25th. Chairman Chen decided to personally attend and break ground. It is reported that the total cost of the waterway dredging project is 240,000 yuan, and approximately 80,000 laborers are conscripted from the provincial capital, and more than 10,000 from Minhou County. (Central News Agency dispatch, 18th)

(Fuzhou) The waterway dredging commencement ceremony is scheduled for the 25th. Chen Yi plans to personally attend and break ground. The total project requires 240,000 workdays, conscripting laborers from the provincial capital, 80,000, and from Minhou County, 20,000, totaling 100,000 people. Each person is required to work for three days. Except for military police agencies and personnel actually on duty, all males have the obligation to work or pay for a substitute. Civil servants should pay a substitute fee, which will be deducted monthly by the provincial government. The provincial Public Security Bureau has been ordered to hire 500 rickshaw pullers by the 24th to form a river-opening team to supplement the labor force. The first waterways to be dredged are Shuibu Men and Jin'an Bridge. (Special dispatch, 18th)

Fujian Civil Affairs Department Plans to Establish District Offices

(Fuzhou) The Civil Affairs Department believes that although there are district offices in various counties of the province, they have not been able to effectively promote self-government and are merely symbolic. It has decided to restructure them into district administrative offices according to the regulations of the Jiangxi Pacification Headquarters and establish a district political training institute to cultivate district chief talents. A plan has been drafted and will be submitted to the next provincial government standing committee meeting for discussion and approval before implementation. (Central News Agency dispatch, 18th)

Japanese National Shot in Changli

Japanese Side Believes the Incident is Serious

Tao Shangming Returns to Tangshan to Investigate the Truth

Tianjin Correspondence. Tao Shangming, Special Commissioner of the Yulian District, hurriedly returned to Tangshan from Tianjin this afternoon. Before leaving, he visited the Japanese Consulate in Tianjin and met with Japanese Vice Consul Tanaka Shotaro to exchange opinions on the recent Konno incident in Changli. After returning to Tangshan, he will discuss the matter with Watanabe, the Deputy Consul of the Tianjin Japanese Consulate Branch stationed in Tangshan. The Japanese side believes that the Konno incident is serious, similar to the Miyakoshi incident that occurred in Yutian last year. The Tianjin Japanese Consulate has ordered Sato, the Chief of the Shanhai Pass Police Branch, to lead patrol chiefs and patrols, and dispatched several senior criminal officers to Changli, the site of the incident, to investigate the perpetrators and investigate the case. At the same time, the Tianjin Japanese Consulate dispatched Owa, the Director of the Judicial System of the Tianjin Police Department, and Chao Jih-sheng-ying-nei to assist Sato in investigating the case. Japanese agencies such as the Changli Japanese Army Garrison and the Shanhai Pass County Gendarmerie Branch Office have each sent specialists to handle the case. Tianjin Japanese newspapers have expanded their publicity of the matter, describing it as an unstable act by the Changli County Security Team and the militia, endangering the lives and property of Japanese residents, and urging the Japanese army to take immediate action, causing panic and widespread fear in Changli. According to reports, the cause of this incident is that Marusan Yoko, located on Erdao Street in Changli City, is owned by a Japanese national named Konno Kanekura. Konno specializes in colluding with Japanese and Korean rogues to sell drugs. On the 4th of this month, he was ambushed by a Korean rogue due to unequal distribution of spoils. At the time, Konno happened to be urinating and was spared by hiding in the toilet. Afterwards, Konno reported to the County Government, resolutely demanding the search and arrest of the Korean and his delivery to the Japanese side, or his extradition and punishment by the Japanese side. Although the County Government had tried its best to search, the Korean had long since fled after failing in the ambush.

Gold and Silver: London gold price rose 2.5 pence today to 142 shillings and 1.5 pence.

British silver London silver price fell 0.0625 today, spot price is 24.5625 pence, futures is 24.6875 pence. India sold, while the United States and speculators bought in. Market conditions are stable.

Indian silver: The Bombay silver market remained calm today. The closing price for spot was 64 rupees and 6 annas, a drop of 4 annas.

Exchange Rate: Anglo-American The London foreign exchange market had very little trading this morning. The opening Anglo-American exchange rate was 4.879375 yuan, lower than yesterday's closing rate of 0.0625. Fluctuations were narrow before noon, and the latest price was 4.881875 yuan, 25 points higher than the opening price. Also, one US dollar is equivalent to 4 shillings and 1.161 pence of British gold.

British-French: The opening price remained unchanged at 74 francs 28, and only fell 13 pounds in the afternoon to 74 francs 15, with no further changes. Anglo-American: The New York foreign exchange market, the opening Anglo-American exchange rate was 4.88 yuan, the same as yesterday's price, then rose 125 points to 4.88125 yuan.

Cotton and Wheat: American cotton The announcement of the Peng Haide case cotton production quota can be seen as beneficial to the multilateral side, and the method of subsidizing those who continue to reduce cotton fields is especially beneficial to the multilateral side, so the cotton market opening price is stable, rising 3 to 5 points. However, after the market price rose, recent purchasers sold one after another, and the market price was affected by this, falling about 6 pounds. Fortunately, the sentiment is still stable, and prices fluctuate, hovering around yesterday's closing price.

Indian cotton: Bombay cotton market, due to large-scale purchases by futures traders and replenishment by shorts, cotton prices soared, and the closing market was strong. The price of White Luo Zhi cotton for the April-May period was 249.5 rupees, a rise of 7.75 rupees. British cotton: Liverpool cotton market rose today due to the improvement in the New York cotton market yesterday. At 1:00 PM, the May period price was 6.88, 8 points higher than yesterday's price.

British wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was more stable today. At 1:00 PM, the May period price was 5 shillings 0.375, half a penny higher. British wheat: The wheat market opened steadily. The price rose slightly because of the strong Liverpool telegram and the report of increasingly cold weather in the northern wheat area. There is a rumor that the East is now buying Australian wheat.

Rubber: London The London rubber market was quiet this morning. The transaction price for the April-June period in the afternoon was 6.5625 pence, 0.0625 lower than yesterday's price.

New York New York rubber fell 10 points at the opening due to the slightly lower London market price, and there was no change within an hour afterwards.

The factor unfavorable to the market conditions is the lack of enterprising spirit when the gold bar dispute is not resolved. The securities opened steadily this morning, and the trend is mostly upward, but the prices of several important stocks, such as US Steel and American Telephone and Telegraph, loosened. There is an image of gradual restoration of trust in the market situation, but it is expected that transactions will not go beyond a narrow range for the time being. Various prices are as follows:

He reported this to the Japanese Gendarmerie Branch Office stationed in the county. The sergeant of the branch office questioned our side. Then, on the 8th of this month, Konno took drugs to Luo County to sell. Just fifteen li outside the north gate of Changli, in a place called Xiaoyingzi, he suddenly encountered two Koreans who jumped out and ambushed him. They fired three shots in a row. Two bullets hit Konno's buttocks, and one bullet hit his left temple, causing heavy bleeding and causing him to collapse to the ground. The two Koreans then searched his body for all his belongings and fled. Later, a villager discovered Konno lying in a pool of blood and rushed to report to the nearby militia defense station. The station carried him away on a stretcher and transferred him to the County Government. This was later heard by the Japanese Army Garrison, who then carried him to the garrison and transported him to Tianjin overnight, where he was admitted to the Japanese Kyowa Hospital for treatment. Although his injuries were serious, they were not fatal. It has been ten days, and there has been no change. The Japanese side was unable to obtain Konno's confession, and strongly claimed that this was done by the Liu Zuozhou's Unit, the First General Team of the War Zone Security Force stationed in Luo County, and the local militia of the county. They said that the previous ambush he suffered in Luo County was also done by Liu's unit, and that Liu's unit had suspected him of selling drugs and demanding kickbacks, and had thus harmed him. They said that he had more than 800 yuan in cash and several pieces of jewelry on his person, which were all looted. The Japanese side took this as fact and the Tangshan Japanese Vice Consul Watanabe lodged a protest to Tao Shangming. Tao planned to send personnel to cooperate with Changli County Magistrate Wan Yi to conduct an investigation after returning to Tangshan, and then proceed with the handling. After this incident occurred, in addition to dismissing the heads of the security team and police station at the site of the incident, County Magistrate Wan dispatched a large number of detectives to investigate the murder separately. This matter was still swirling, when on the 13th of this month, between Qinhuangdao and Shimen, a Korean rogue riding in a long-distance bus also refused to pay the fare and refused to listen to the security team's inspection, resulting in a conflict and brawl. The Japanese side also claimed that Liu Zuozhou's unit was intentionally making trouble for the Japanese and Koreans, and filed a protest on both matters. (15th)

He Yingqin Returns to Beiping

Will Travel Between Nanjing and Beiping Frequently in the Future

Huang Fu Departs South in Eastern Attire After Meeting He

Beiping Correspondence: He Yingqin, Chairman of the Beiping Military Sub-Council, returned south from Beiping on October 7th of last year to manage the affairs of the Ministry of Military Administration. He traveled north on the 9th of this month, representing Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to attend the memorial ceremony for the late Mr. Yan in Taiyuan. Having completed these affairs, he departed from Taiyuan on the 16th at noon and arrived in Beiping. Upon hearing this news, various Party, military, and political organizations in Beiping City immediately began preparations for a welcome. At dawn today (the 17th), the West Railway Station was guarded by the Beiping City Public Security Bureau's Security Team, the Ministry of Military Administration's Special Service Regiment, the Special Service Company, the Central Military Police Third Regiment, the Beiping Military Police Command, and other military and police forces. Temporary cordons were set up along the route from the station to the Jurentang Hall. A sign-in book was placed in front of the station gate. Those who signed in included Zhang Jianchu, representing Huang Fu; Yu Jiaji, representing the Political Reorganization Council; Shang Zhen, Wan Fulin, Song Zheyuan, Qin Dechun, He Jingwu, Bao Wenwei, Men Zhizhong, Pang Bingxun, Ji Yiqiao, and other members of the Military Sub-Council, as well as chiefs of various departments and sections above the rank of major, heads of various military offices stationed in Beiping, Beiping Mayor Yuan Liang and the heads of various bureaus, Zhan Zhaoyang and Xun Lin representing the provincial and municipal Party headquarters, Leng Jiaji and Wang Zhuoran representing business and academic circles, and others. The municipal Party headquarters also posted welcome banners. He Yingqin left Taiyuan at noon on the 16th by a regular train, arriving in Shijiazhuang at 8 PM that evening. He transferred to a chartered train, departing Shijiazhuang around 10 PM. As it was late when passing through Baoding, he did not disembark but met with key personnel from the Xingying in the train. He continued his journey at 0:10 AM this morning (the 17th), arriving at Xibianmen around 6 AM and reaching Beiping at 7:25 AM. After alighting from the train, He shook hands with the welcoming personnel to express his gratitude and then returned to the Jurentang Hall by car. Those who accompanied He included Secretary Xie Zhongnan, Zeng Jingcang, Military Sub-Council member Liu Yifei, Counselor Hou Cheng, Section Chief Zhu Shiqin, and several others. Around 9 AM, Military Sub-Council members Shang Zhen, Wan Fulin, Bao Wenwei, Song Zheyuan, Qin Dechun, Pang Bingxun, Men Zhizhong, He Jingwu, Bao Yulin, and others led the staff members above the rank of school officer from various departments and sections to the Jurentang Hall for an audience. Around 10 AM, Huang Fu visited and had a long conversation, departing only at noon. On the same day, He issued a written statement as follows: "Last year, as I had been away from Nanjing for a long time, there were many matters in the Ministry of Military Administration that needed to be addressed. I went from Beiping to Nanjing in October, taking the opportunity to attend the funeral of my mother-in-law, Madam Wang, in Shanghai. Later, due to the convening of the Fifth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, I stayed in Nanjing to attend the meeting, residing there for nearly three months. Recently, the affairs of the Ministry have been largely organized, so I left Nanjing and traveled north on the 9th of this month, also detouring to Hebian Village to offer sacrifices to the late Mr. Yan on behalf of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. The funeral arrangements for the late Mr. Yan were completed on the 14th, and I departed from Taiyuan yesterday afternoon to return to Beiping. I found that Shanxi Province is making great efforts in production and construction, with excellent results. The Tongpu Railway, which is being built by the Shanxi provincial armory, has already opened to traffic as far as Xinzhou in the north and as far as Huozhou in the south. It is said that the entire line will be open to traffic next year. Shanxi Province has been vigorously promoting domestic goods in recent years, especially products from Shanxi and Suiyuan, which is an excellent phenomenon. The people of the country should unite and promote domestic goods in this spirit, which will greatly benefit the national economy. Since the Red Army bandits in Jiangxi had their old nest in Ruijin destroyed, they have successively fled westward. Although they were intercepted by government troops along the way, a portion still took the opportunity to flee into Guizhou Province, attempting to link up with the Red Army bandits in Sichuan. The Central Government now has a complete plan for suppressing the bandits in Sichuan and Guizhou, aiming to thoroughly eliminate them in the shortest possible time. As the affairs of the Ministry of Military Administration and the Military Sub-Council are both very important, I may travel between Beiping and Nanjing frequently in the future to handle all important public matters."

After being appointed concurrently as Minister of the Interior, Huang Fu originally intended to go to Nanjing as soon as possible to take office. However, due to the need for someone to be stationed in the north, his departure was delayed. Now that He Yingqin has arrived in Beiping, he is scheduled to depart south by plane tomorrow (the 18th). His luggage has already been dispatched by personnel at 6:50 PM this evening (the 17th). It is also said that the Ford plane sent to Beiping for Huang's use has landed in Qingdao today (the 17th) due to weather conditions and is expected to arrive in Beiping at noon tomorrow (the 18th). Based on this, it is speculated that Huang's departure will be delayed until the day after tomorrow (the 19th). Chairman Yu Xuezhong of Hebei Province arrived in Beiping by car from Tianjin at 4 PM this afternoon (the 17th) to visit He and see Huang off. He went to the Jurentang Hall that night to meet with He to report on matters and is scheduled to visit Huang at the Political Reorganization Council tomorrow morning (the 18th) to seek instructions on all matters (the 17th).

Guangzhou City Organizes Winter Relief Association to Provide Relief

Ten Measures Established

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, as it is now deep winter in Guangzhou, the poor are huddled on the streets, lacking clothing and food, in a truly miserable state. The Winter Relief Association was established some days ago. A vacant lot was selected to build sheds to house the homeless poor, and the following measures for providing relief during the cold weather were established: (1) When the thermometer drops below 51 degrees Fahrenheit, congee distribution will begin; (2) The rice for congee will be red rice and broken rice; (3) The rice, oil, salt, ginger, and vegetables for congee will be purchased by the Relief Association; (4) The organizations responsible for cooking the congee will be: Fangbian Hospital in the Dongdi District, Chongzheng Shantang in the Huangsha District, and Aiyu Shantang and Huixing Shantang in the Haizhu District; (5) Cooking utensils will be borrowed from various Shantangs; (6) The food and wages for the cooks will be handled by the Relief Department; (7) Congee distribution will be limited to residents within the sheds; (8) Two teapots will be set up in each shed for those who are thirsty, and the workers in charge of the teapots will be hired by the Association, with the teapots borrowed from Shantangs; (9) The method for distributing cotton-padded clothing will be determined by the Relief Department; (10) The purchase and quantity of cotton-padded clothing will be determined based on the situation (the 12th).

Songjiang: Continued Discussion on Dredging the City River. The city river within the county seat has been silted up for a long time and urgently needs to be dredged. Construction was started once last year, but it was suspended due to poor management and disputes among local residents. Now, the county government has ordered Li Zufu, the head of the First District, to continue the work to fulfill the people's expectations. Regarding the dredging expenses, the public voluntarily contributes. In addition to businesses, the county chamber of commerce has convened meetings to assign members to be responsible for fundraising in sections. For households, the heads of various towns will work with the section offices in each section to raise funds, aiming to collect 8,000 yuan. If it is not enough, a request will be made to the provincial government for assistance. Yesterday (the 17th), Director Li also convened a meeting of the heads of various sections, resolving to start construction in the first section in the middle of next month. The construction of dams and water diversion projects in each section will be contracted by workers, with cost estimates submitted to the district and town offices for review and approval. The recruitment of river workers will also be based on the principle of employing local people, and the recruitment method will also be managed by the district office. The expenses for supervisors and laborers required by each section office will be limited to 60 yuan as a resolution. During the discussions, Director Li led the staff to survey the location of the dam construction to facilitate statistics.

On September 5th of last year, the Supervisory Office of the County Public Security Bureau discovered Chen Shaokun and his wife, Chen Zhu, selling poison pills at No. 9 Nanyang Lane. Upon detailed interrogation, they confessed that the poison pills they sold were purchased from Wang Guiqing, a resident of No. 3 Silangjun Temple Lane in the city. They also found pill-making equipment in the Xue residence across the street. Due to the crowding of prisoners, the eight people, including the former Chen Shaokun, were sent back to the county government of this county yesterday for detention, pending approval for execution. The main criminal, Wang Guiqing, is still to be strictly arrested and brought to justice. It is said that none of the convicted criminals were sentenced to death, but all were given fixed-term imprisonment.

Changshu Labor Relief Dredging to Commence

This county suffered a severe drought last summer, and now that winter has arrived, famine riots have repeatedly occurred in various rural areas, demanding winter relief. As the county government has no dedicated funds, the County Administrative Council decided to organize a labor relief dredging project to dredge the city rivers in various rural areas to facilitate transportation and provide work relief. The county government has made every effort to plan and establish a project office, with the county magistrate serving as the director and the district chiefs serving as the deputy directors. Supervisors will be hired by the employees of each district. As for the labor recruitment method, thirty people will form a platoon, ten platoons will form a group, and three groups will form a team, with platoon, group, and team leaders appointed by the township heads, with appropriate subsidies. The project is planned for three months, and in addition to the 10,000 yuan approved by the provincial government, the shortfall will be raised locally. The measures have now been submitted by the county government to the Construction Department for approval. Once approved, work can begin, which is expected to be in late this month.

Yangzhou: Gong Sheng Small Wheel Hits Rock and Sinks

The Huai River Diversion Engineering Office hired the Gong Sheng small wheel on the morning of the 16th to transport foreign pine from Zhenjiang to Shaobo. When it arrived at the Dawang Temple section outside the south gate of Yangzhou, it struck a rock in the water due to the many sailboats lining the north bank. The boiler was immediately flooded, and the ship tilted slightly and gradually sank into the water. The crew immediately tried to move the rice and other materials ashore and telegraphed the company to arrange for salvage.

Zhejiang Public Debt Collateral Loan of 2 Million Yuan Draft Contract Agreed Yesterday

Borrowed from the Bank of China and Other Banks at 1% Weekly Interest

Contract to be Signed After Agreement, Loan to be Released on the 25th

Xin Xin News reports: The Zhejiang Provincial Government is mortgaging local public debt to Shanghai banking circles for a loan. As a result of Finance Director Xu Qingfu's negotiations in Shanghai, the banking community has agreed to lend 2 million yuan first, which will be undertaken by a syndicate of fourteen banks, including the Bank of China. A meeting was held on the third floor of the Bank of China yesterday morning, and the draft loan contract was decided. Xu took it back to the provincial government for reporting last night. Once passed, it can be formally signed in Shanghai, and the loan will be released on the 25th of this month, to be repaid in five years. The details are as follows:

Negotiation Process

The Zhejiang Provincial Government urgently needs to carry out various work relief construction and debt restructuring projects. In addition, the drought last year sharply reduced tax revenue, and the province is facing financial difficulties. It was decided to pledge 10 million yuan of local public debt issued in 1934 to Shanghai banking circles for 6 million yuan in cash for application. Finance Director Xu Qingfu was sent to Shanghai to conduct negotiations. Since arriving in Shanghai last week, Xu has held consultations with leaders of various banks and hosted a banquet for the banking community to discuss the matter as a whole. As a result of the discussions, the banks felt that the Lunar New Year was approaching, and it was difficult to accept the full amount of 6 million yuan, so they unanimously voted to temporarily borrow 2 million yuan, with the remaining 4 million yuan to be discussed later. After the amount was decided by both parties, it was decided to hold a meeting yesterday to discuss the loan contract.

Meeting Discussion

At 10 AM yesterday morning, Xu invited representatives of various lending banks to hold a formal meeting in the conference room of the General Management Office on the third floor of the Bank of China to discuss the loan contract. Those present included Chen Muhao, Manager of the Shanghai branch of the Bank of China; Jin Runquan, Manager of the Hangzhou branch; Zhang Peishen of the Bank of Communications; Yang Jiemei of the Shanghai Bank; Ye Fuxiao of the Continental Bank; Hu Bijiang of the Zhongnan Bank; Wang Boyuan of the Siming Bank; Fu Xiaoan of the Bank of Communications; Wu Yunzhai of the Jincheng Bank; Xu Xinliu of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank; Wang Zhihua of the Xinhua Bank; Li Fuxun of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank; and Xu Qingfu, Director of Finance of Zhejiang, and others, totaling more than ten people. After Xu Qingfu, as chairman, explained everything, they immediately began to discuss the contract clauses, and the meeting adjourned at 12 noon.

Contract Highlights

Xin Xin News reporters learned that as a result of yesterday's meeting, all the clauses of the contract have been fully agreed upon. The various measures are roughly the same as the previous 3 million loan. The key points are: (1) The total mortgage amount is 2 million yuan; (2) The guarantee fund includes Zhejiang Province's business tax, land tax, and brokerage tax; (3) The interest rate is 1% per week; (4) The term is five years, with the principal and interest fully repaid by the end of 1939; (5) The principal and interest will be repaid twice a year, at the end of June and the end of December. The detailed clauses will be announced after the formal signing.

Organization of Banking Syndicate: The loan is being undertaken by fourteen banks, including the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, Siming Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Continental Bank, Yanyeh Bank, Jincheng Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Bank of Communications, Xinhua Bank, Guohua Bank, and Guohuo Bank. The amount borrowed by each bank is the same as the previous loan distribution. For the convenience of payment, the banks have specially organized a banking syndicate to handle it, and the Bank of China has been designated as the representative of the banking syndicate, responsible for presiding over all matters such as payment.

Xu Returns to Hangzhou: Finance Director Xu Qingfu took the draft contract on the Shanghai-Hangzhou express train back to Hangzhou at 5 PM yesterday, after successfully negotiating the loan contract in Shanghai, to report the progress to the Zhejiang Provincial Government. Once approved by the provincial government, he will return to Shanghai to distribute the contract to the banks for formal signing. It is reported that the lending banks have decided that the Zhejiang Provincial Government urgently needs to use the loan, and it has now been decided to transfer the loan to the Bank of China, the representative of the banking syndicate, on the 25th of this month, and then the Hangzhou branch of the Bank of China will transfer it to the Zhejiang Finance Department for application.

Five Exchanges Sent Representatives to Nanjing Yesterday

To Participate in Finance and Economics Conferences

Shiye News reports: The Ministry of Finance has decided to start collecting exchange taxes from February 1st. The details are as follows:

Representatives of Five Exchanges Go to Nanjing

Securities Requests Exemption from Taxation

The Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange believes that although the Ministry of Finance's collection of exchange taxes applies to the Shanghai exchanges in general, all of the exchange's usual operations involve government bonds, which are close to physical trading, and should not be taxed in the same way as other exchanges. It specifically telegraphed the Central Political Consultative Conference in Nanjing, the National Government, and various ministries and departments, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters yesterday, requesting exemption from taxation to maintain commerce. The original petition stated: (Titles omitted) Respectful Greetings,

Polish Rejection of Chinese Goods: Chamber of Commerce Cables for External Intervention

Chinese Goods Transported to Poland Should Receive the Same Treatment as Other Countries

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday cabled the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, according to a letter from Wu Zemin, a merchant residing in Poland, he has been living in Poland for many years, engaged in the business of selling retail goods. Previously, the hand-woven straw baskets of our country were quite popular among the Polish people. In the winter of 1933, he entrusted Shanghai Xinda Li to purchase two boxes, totaling one hundred and eighty-two sets, valued at over 170 silver dollars, to be transported to Poland for sale. However, after arriving at the port, the customs officials of that country, disregarding international credibility, arbitrarily raised tariffs. Each set of three straw baskets, with a cost price of less than one Chinese currency dollar, was taxed three times that amount. According to the original Sino-Polish Commercial Treaty, Chinese goods transported to Poland should be taxed according to the most-favored-nation treatment. However, the tax levied on straw baskets transported from Czechoslovakia to Poland is less than eighty percent of their value. The difference is vast. Their violation of the commercial treaty and disregard for national rights are evident. After repeated petitions to diplomatic officials and local lawyers to argue reasonably, it was to no avail, as that country intentionally excludes Chinese goods, turning a deaf ear to all appeals, ultimately making it impossible to import and allowing them to be confiscated. The loss to the individual merchant is minimal and not worth mentioning. However, considering the decline of our national power and the various abuses suffered by overseas Chinese in their host countries, as well as the arbitrary exclusion of Chinese goods, the number of such cases is countless. The reason why they endure humiliation and do not report their plight to fellow Chinese is that they lack sufficient understanding of the domestic situation. There are few who can accurately convey their experiences, causing the suffering of overseas Chinese to be buried without being heard, and the sales of domestic goods to become increasingly sluggish. Now that the Sino-Polish Commercial Treaty is about to be revised, we earnestly hope that our government and people of society will rise up and strive to prevent the recurrence of similar incidents, so as to safeguard national rights and alleviate the difficulties of merchants. The overseas Chinese would be very grateful," etc.

The Chamber also stated, "Our country and Poland have long established a treaty of amity and commerce. Goods from that country entering China are taxed in accordance with the most-favored-nation treatment, the same as other countries. Why is there differential treatment for the export of Chinese goods to their country? Chinese merchants operating in Europe not only have small capital and weak foundations, but also face long journeys, completely different languages and customs, making it difficult for them to gain access. Their situation is different from that in North America and the South Seas Islands. If this overseas Chinese merchant has been traveling to Poland for many years and can purchase goods from China for sale, it is a groundbreaking event in the history of foreign trade. Such nascent businesses should be carefully protected. We cannot remain silent because the amounts are small, allowing the customs officials of that country to continue their old ways, causing Chinese goods to disappear from there altogether. We should ask your Ministry to argue reasonably to ensure that the commercial activities of this overseas Chinese merchant in Poland and the future transportation routes for Chinese goods to Poland will not be obstructed. This is in the public interest. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce respectfully petitions, Xiao."

Previously, there was a proposal by the Ministry of Finance to levy a transaction tax. We have already presented the situation and appealed for consideration of the merchants' difficulties, requesting the immediate withdrawal of the tax proposal. Recently, it has been reported that the tax proposal has been submitted by the Ministry of Finance to the Executive Yuan and then to the Legislative Yuan for review by the Finance and Economic Committee. Upon hearing this news, the public is anxious. We believe that while the collection of transaction tax is not without precedent in other countries, it is a first for our country. The economic structures of various countries are different, and the commercial situations vary. Therefore, the tax procedures must be adapted to the circumstances and suit the national conditions. It is not appropriate to force a fit. From the perspective of our country's history, the former Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce of the Northern Government once promulgated the "Regulations on Exchange Tax" in September of the 15th year of the Republic of China, but it was later abolished due to the change of government. The Ministry of Finance revised and promulgated it in August of the 16th year, but it was never implemented. Later, the Financial Consolidation Bureau of the Ministry of Finance was established and drafted a plan, which was submitted by various exchanges in Shanghai to abolish the "Regulations on Exchange Tax." The Ministry of Finance reluctantly approved a delay in implementation (as stated in the original report of the Ministry of Finance to the Executive Yuan), which proves that the relationship of this case is very important. In recent years, floods, droughts, and banditry have led to rural bankruptcy, urban poverty, industrial and commercial failures, and a lack of savings. After the January 28th Incident, the people were impoverished and resources exhausted, making it even more unsustainable. The government has always been mindful of the people's suffering and granted consideration. However, the current economic situation is deteriorating. Discussing recovery, the timing for imposing exchange tax is not yet ripe. We have always admired our government authorities for considering the people's livelihood and protecting enterprises, and we believe that they will not bear to further burden the people at this time of economic decline. Moreover, transaction tax and exchange tax, one levied on both parties of the transaction and the other levied on the exchange, seem to be two different things on the surface, but in reality, both are operated by brokers. If exchange tax has already been levied and transaction tax is added, the amount will be reduced, transactions will decrease, and the operation of brokers will be directly affected, which will indirectly reduce the collection of exchange tax, forming a chain reaction. Those who seek to increase revenue may not be able to expand revenue. We should ask your councils, the Executive Yuan, and the ministries to continue to approve the original plan of the 16th year for the transaction tax case and postpone the review. Furthermore, the draft "Regulations on Transaction Tax" of the Ministry of Finance is largely based on the revised "Transaction Tax Law" of Japan in April of the 11th year of Taisho. According to the provisions of that law, transactions of goods and transactions of national debt securities are not taxed. Since transactions outside of the goods exchange are not taxed, because the place of purchase and sale is within the exchange, it is used as the reason for taxation. We are deeply afraid that the buyer and seller will regard the exchange as a long journey, the exchange's business will plummet, and the collection of transaction tax will also be greatly affected. This can be asserted. The mission of buying and selling national debt coupons is the expression of the people's trust in the government. The mission of the exchange is to facilitate the circulation of securities on the one hand and to consolidate the country's credit on the other. The situation is completely different from ordinary goods. If the same tax is levied, it is no different from making the people fulfill an obligation that should not be made outside of subscribing to national debts. In terms of sentiment and law, I am afraid that friendly countries will laugh, and as a result, bond stagnation will be brewed, and new bonds will not be easy to promote. The danger is unimaginable. Therefore, the Japanese tax law stipulates that national debt transactions are specifically listed as tax-free. We find that the draft plan of the Ministry of Finance does not specify whether the purchase and sale of national debt coupons should be taxed. We are very worried about comparisons and references. Its currency flow is sufficient to damage national credit and reduce treasury revenue. The exchanges that have just sprouted will be hit hard, and the brokers in the storm will also be difficult to maintain. We should ask your councils, the Executive Yuan, and the ministries to maintain the original plan of the 16th year for the transaction tax case and postpone the review. To sum up, the exchange tax has been implemented for a long time. The securities exchange part pays more than 200,000 yuan in taxes every year. It is not powerless to repay the country. We should ask your councils, the Executive Yuan, and the ministries to consider the great importance of national plan and people's livelihood, and allow the tax case to be reviewed slowly, in order to comply with the feelings and sympathize with the merchants' difficulties. The urgent telegram is pressing, and we are extremely eager to await orders. Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange Broker Association Representatives Wang Zhengruo, Wu Limen, Zhu Anfu respectfully petitions.

The Municipal Farmers' Association Asks to Maintain Cotton Futures Trading

The Municipal Farmers' Association yesterday submitted a report to the Social Affairs Bureau, stating: "Reporting on the matter of forwarding a report. According to the Yangsi District Farmers' Association, 'Reporting on the matter of stopping cotton futures trading, which is detrimental to the rural economy. Requesting that it be maintained as usual to reassure the farmers.' Recently, newspapers and dramas reported that a few yarn factories requested the prohibition of cotton futures trading on the Chinese Yarn and Cloth Exchange to alleviate the situation due to the high price of cotton and the low price of yarn. After reading it, we were deeply surprised. The price of cotton is always determined by the trend of supply and demand. If supply is less than demand, the price will be high; otherwise, it will be low. Moreover, the exchange was originally established to regulate supply and demand and equalize prices. The daily market price must be determined in accordance with the law and cannot be manipulated or monopolized by a few people. This is clear. Cotton is our country's major agricultural product and the farmers' major income. The level of its price is of great importance to the rural economy. Moreover, the price of cotton in our country is the lowest in the world. How can we further depress it to exploit farmers' income and hinder the rural economy? Recently, our government has spared no effort in rescuing farmers and revitalizing the countryside. However, these manufacturers, using losses as an excuse, disregard the government's intentions and listen to alarming words, insisting on depressing cotton prices to achieve their selfish goals. If trading is stopped, goods will be blocked, the economy will be cut off, and the farmers will suffer. How can this be tolerated? We feel uneasy and cannot remain silent. We should submit a document to your council for review and approval, and then forward it to the competent Yuan and Ministry to instruct the Chinese Yarn and Cloth Exchange to maintain cotton futures trading as usual to reassure the farmers. This is in the public interest." Based on this, we believe that the standard of cotton price should be based on the amount of supply and demand, which is of great importance to the farmers' economy, and cannot be monopolized for the benefit of a few manufacturers. According to the previous report, we should prepare a document to forward it. We look forward to your review and forwarding, as this is in the public interest.
