Municipal Federation Submits to Various Organizations, Striving for Extension of the Liquidation Period

Stating That Without Postponing Rent Payments, Bankruptcies Are Inevitable

The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation cabled to the following organizations yesterday to address the city's economic problems: the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party in Nanjing, Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan, Chairman Chiang of the Military Affairs Commission, Mayor Wu of the Shanghai Municipal Government, Director Wu of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Shanghai Concession, the Shanghai Banking Association, and various other organizations and groups, stating: "The economic situation in Shanghai is bleak, and the decline of industry and commerce has reached an extreme point. Company failures and liquidations are a daily occurrence. Due to currency tightening, falling prices, unsold goods, high rents, and sluggish finances, nine out of ten are losing money. If rescue measures are not taken, widespread closures are inevitable, and prosperous Shanghai will become a dead city. We are filled with trepidation at the looming crisis. Our Federation, as a group of citizens, has a clearer understanding of the situation. In accordance with our duties, we convened a temporary representative meeting on January 16 to discuss the situation. It was agreed that extraordinary measures should be taken in response to extraordinary events. Extending the liquidation period is essential for recovery, postponing rent payments is essential to avoid bankruptcies, reducing housing taxes is essential to reduce expenses, and levying housing taxes on vacant houses is essential to offset the reduction in housing taxes. We also urge rent reductions. As a result, the following resolutions were made: (A) Extend the period of industrial and commercial liquidation for one year, with interest paid as usual. (1) Issue a declaration. (2) Submit a report to the Party and government agencies for approval. Send letters to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to carry out the project. (B) Submit a report to the Executive Yuan, instructing the Ministry of Finance to allocate loans from the Central Bank to rescue Shanghai's industry and commerce. (C) (1) Submit a report to the Municipal Government and send a letter to the Public Works Department, requesting the levying of housing taxes on vacant houses. (2) Submit a report to the competent authorities to issue an order postponing rent payments for six months. Submit a report to the Municipal Government and send a letter to the Taxpayers' Association to reduce housing taxes. This is recorded in the file. This matter concerns the rise and fall of Shanghai's economy. Therefore, we send a telegram requesting investigation and implementation. Three and a half million Shanghai citizens depend on it. The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation respectfully petitions, Hao."

X X X X

Ye Jiaxing, Standing Committee Member of the Municipal Federation, Discusses Countermeasures to Revive the Economy

Plant Liquidations Due to Rural Bankruptcy and Sharp Decline in Purchasing Power

From Industry Solidarity to Avoid Speculation

The New Voice Agency reported: "The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation recently issued a declaration on reviving the economy, advocating for a one-year extension of industrial and commercial liquidation, with interest paid as usual, and postponement of rent payments, etc. This has attracted attention from people in society. Ye Jiaxing, a standing committee member of the Federation, expressed his views to a reporter from the New Voice Agency yesterday, stating that although he attended the Federation's standing committee meeting the other day, the agenda was to discuss the articles of association. The issue of reviving the economy was not specifically addressed. Later, he left due to other matters. Regarding this issue, he deeply believes that the decline of commerce and the economic downturn throughout the country are due to rural bankruptcy and the sharp decline in people's purchasing power. The floods in the north and droughts in the south last year exacerbated the severity of the symptoms, just like a person suffering from phlegm who is also suffering from an external infection. For the present plan, he believes that the only way is to do our best to revive the rural areas, increase the people's purchasing power, so that various domestic products can be sold smoothly, and to open up international trade places, so that there can be a way out for foreign countries. This is the fundamental remedy for reviving the national economy. As for the decline of the city's economy and the decline of commerce, in addition to the above reasons, there are other factors. One of them is that the same industry is fighting each other and destroying each other. For example, in the rubber industry a few years ago, there were only seven or eight rubber factories in the city, and their business was very good and they were all able to make profits. However, in the past one or two years, the establishment of rubber factories has mushroomed, increasing to forty or fifty. As a result, the factories are fighting each other and competing by lowering prices. There is no spirit of unity among the same industry, and they are doing their best to commit suicide. This is the case in the rubber industry, and other industries are also the same. No wonder the market is in decline. Furthermore, several large stores in the city have recently gone bankrupt. The reason for their bankruptcy is not the failure of the store's own business, but its concurrent operation of businesses other than the store's business. The recent bankruptcy of Tai Company is a clear example of this. Secondly, the managers of stores in the city often use their managerial position to engage in speculative activities privately. The lucky ones create personal wealth, but the stores themselves do not benefit. The unlucky ones often cannot make ends meet and move the store's money without authorization, causing the store to run aground or go bankrupt. There are many such things. Therefore, he sincerely hopes that the business community in the city can strive to unite the same industry, avoid operating foreign businesses and speculative businesses, and then the revival of the economy will be greatly assisted. Furthermore, last year all industries have declared liquidation. It is expected that after the summary relief, there will be a new innovative and emerging business. Recalling that the Civil Code drafted by the Legislative Yuan had a draft for joint shops to be jointly and severally liable, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has strived for the amendment of the Commercial Registration Law to supplement it. This registration law is extremely important for emerging joint stores. I hope that the legislative authorities will promulgate it as soon as possible to benefit the city's commerce."

Therefore, based on this theory, they believe that the claim that the situation in Chahar is tense is a rumor from the outside. However, the telegram stated that Xiao Zhenying's inspection of eastern Chahar showed that the Japanese troops had no activity, but were quite active. It is not possible to prove whether the Japanese Embassy really had not heard anything about it."

Lunar Eclipse Tonight, Reaches Full Roundness Tomorrow Morning

Total Eclipse Visible in Shanghai

According to the report from the Xujiahui Observatory, the total eclipse visible in Shanghai between tonight and tomorrow morning, the beginning of the eclipse can be seen in Eastern Europe, Asia, Australia, the eastern part of the Indian Ocean, the Pacific Ocean, and the western part of the North America. The end of the eclipse can be seen in Europe, Africa (except for the westernmost part), the Indian Ocean, Australia, the northwestern part of the Pacific Ocean, and the northwestern part of North America. Today, Saturday, at 8:39 PM, the moon enters the penumbra, at 9:03 PM it enters the umbra, at 11:03 PM the eclipse begins, tomorrow, Sunday, at 0:31 AM the total eclipse is complete, at 1:41 AM the moon leaves the umbra, at 2:55 AM it leaves the penumbra.

Declaration of the Shanghai Newspaper Workers' Union

In 1927, when the National Revolutionary Army established its presence in Beijing and Shanghai and the mass movement swept the country, our newspaper workers, on the one hand, were wary of our own disunity and lack of organization, and on the other hand, felt that the National Revolution was a revolution of the entire people, and everyone had the right and opportunity to participate in politics. The members of our association, based on the above two reasons, organized this association. Over the years, we have been working with the sincerity and unity of our workers and the principle of labor-capital harmony, striving to increase the status of workers themselves, improve their living conditions, improve their work skills, cultivate the spirit of autonomy, and create workers' spare time schools, so that the children of workers can have the opportunity to attend school. All of these are the consistent propositions of our association, which we have never forgotten.

Since the foreign invasion of September 18, the fall of the Eastern Provinces, the decline of national consciousness throughout the country, and the people's awareness of the urgent need for national disaster, fortunately, the sincerity and unity of the comrades in the central government, their composure and prudence, and their comprehensive plan to deal with the national disaster, the first step must be to settle the internal affairs, and to settle the internal affairs must first eliminate the Communist Party. The recent suppression of the communist bandits in Jiangxi, although it is due to the collapse of the communist theory itself, which is not suitable for China, is also due to the divine wisdom of Chiang Kai-shek and the use of the generals, which has led to the increasingly stable central government, the daily progress of national consciousness, and the hope for the revival of the Chinese nation. The members of our association, adhering to the Three People's Principles, have never forgotten their responsibility to save the country and save the nation. Following the central government's intentions, under the leadership of the Three People's Principles and Chiang Kai-shek, they are working hard to fulfill their responsibility to save the national China. Therefore, at the beginning of the 16th session of the Executive Committee of our association, we hereby announce the propositions of our association, hoping that all sectors will take note of them. Hereby declare, Shanghai Newspaper Workers' Union, January 18, 1935.

Yu Qiaqing Discusses the Resolution of the Shanghai-Ningbo Shipping Route Dispute

The Mingxing Steamer will Initiate Scheduled Service, Temporarily Replacing Xin Jiangtian

An Open Invitation for All Sectors to Visit is Scheduled for the 21st

Xinsheng News Agency reports: The Sanbei Company is the agent for the Mingxing Steamer operating on the Zhenhai route, also serving Wanning and Ningbo. Subsequently, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Ningshao Company separately submitted letters to the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau, requesting the Bureau to suspend the Mingxing Steamer's route permit. The Bureau forwarded these letters to the Sanbei Company, instructing them to respond to the issues raised. Later, Director Peng of the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau invited key personnel from the three companies to a meeting at the Bureau on the 12th of this month to discuss a resolution to this matter. As no announcement was made, people from all walks of life are quite concerned. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency specifically visited Mr. Yu Qiaqing, General Manager of the Sanbei Company, at the company yesterday to inquire about the matter. Mr. Yu was gracious enough to grant an interview and informed the reporter as follows: On the afternoon of the 12th of this month, I (referring to himself) attended a meeting at the invitation of Director Peng of the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau. Present were Mr. Liu Hongsheng, General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and Mr. Yuan Fudeng, Manager of the Ningshao Company. I asked Director Peng whether the meeting would discuss the suspension of the route permit. Director Peng replied that the purpose of the meeting was to discuss cooperation methods among the three companies, not the suspension of the route permit. I then asked the representatives from China Merchants and Ningshao whether they had seen the Sanbei Company's response to the Maritime Affairs Bureau and whether there were any discrepancies that they wished to discuss. Both representatives acknowledged that the facts stated in the Sanbei Company's response were accurate. I then stated that since both of them recognized that the Sanbei Company had a legitimate case, the petition was reasonable. In advanced shipping nations, route permits are only categorized into three types: ocean-going, coastal, and river. There is no restriction like this, and there is no reason to withhold a route permit based on the government's will. Mr. Liu then stated that he had discussed the matter with Minister Zhu, and that during the preparation period for cooperation, if the Mingxing Steamer insisted on sailing between Shanghai and Ningbo, the route permit would have to be suspended. I replied that the Mingxing Steamer sailing between Shanghai and Zhenhai, also serving Wanning and Ningbo, was solely for the purpose of aiding the rural areas and facilitating transportation. I had repeatedly stated that I was willing to sacrifice profits for the sake of this cause and that I embraced the principle of sacrifice. Furthermore, I did not understand which laws or regulations this violated. Was it that if the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company had ships sailing on a route, it should be restricted for others? Even if our (referring to the government) thought we were violating the law, and the company went bankrupt as a result, we would accept it. Moreover, to take a step back, even if the Maritime Affairs Bureau granted the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's wish and suspended the Mingxing's Shanghai-Ningbo route permit, the Sanbei Company could simply park the Mingxing Steamer indefinitely and wait for a fair resolution. Of the other ships in the company's fleet, approximately twenty have permits for the Shanghai-Ningbo route, and it would not be impossible to dispatch one of them to operate the route. Would the Maritime Affairs Bureau revoke all of these route permits as well? Director Peng then reiterated the earlier remarks about cooperation. I was extremely supportive of cooperation, especially since the Mingxing's service to Shanghai-Zhenhai, also serving Wanning-Ningbo, was primarily for rural relief and not for profit. Therefore, if the abolition of transshipment taxes on local goods transported by Chinese ships to treaty ports were achieved, or if a Yangtze River cooperation agreement were reached, the Sanbei Company could suspend the Mingxing Steamer's service between Shanghai and Zhenhai. Mr. Liu stated that the Yangtze River cooperation agreement was expected to be finalized within approximately two months. I replied that that would not be too far off. I would be willing to make peaceful concessions to the extent possible without compromising the principle of rural relief. Mr. Liu then suggested whether the four companies operating between Shanghai and Ningbo could meet again to discuss the matter. I expressed my support, and we went together to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, also inviting representatives from Jardine Matheson to the meeting. It was agreed that the cooperation agreement among the four companies operating between Shanghai and Ningbo would continue, while the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company would be responsible for signing the Yangtze River cooperation agreement within two months. Starting from the 22nd of this month, the Mingxing Steamer would temporarily replace the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xin Jiangtian Steamer for one month. After that, it would replace the Ningshao Company's Xin Ningshao Steamer for another month. If the Yangtze River cooperation agreement was still not finalized after two months, the Sanbei Company would operate the route on its own until the date when the transshipment tax on local goods was abolished, at which point it would switch to operating on the Yangtze River. During the period of substituting for the China Merchants and Ningshao companies, the profits and losses would be borne by each respective company, while the Sanbei Company would only collect rent for the ship. All the ship's crew, staff in the operations department, and cabin attendants would be appointed by the Sanbei Company and could not be changed. The Ningshao Company's Xin Ningshao, serving both Wan and Zhenhai, would dock at the Sanbei Wharf as a resolution. The reporter then asked Mr. Yu that he had been told about the huge relationship with the Shanghai-Zhenhai route, and the rural villages saved; were there any other major relationships, that could be revealed? Qing replied that there were three other points in addition to helping the rural areas by operating the Shanghai-Zhenhai route: First, to reduce the burden of local goods; second, to save time for small passengers; and third, that the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway was about to be completed, so that goods from Zhejiang and Jiangxi provinces could be exported from Zhenhai. Therefore, based on these three points, his company was willing to sacrifice everything. It was inappropriate for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to oppose this. It was also learned that the Mingxing Steamer was scheduled to begin operating on the Xin Jiangtian Steamer's schedule on the 22nd of this month. On the previous day, at 11:00 AM, the Sanbei Company would host a tour of the ship at the Jinliyuan Ningbo Wharf for people from all walks of life.

The Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee Reports that an Entire Family in Haining Died by Suicide

Hoping That All Sectors Will Quickly Offer Assistance

Mr. Wang Yusan, a doctor of political science and sociology who recently arrived in Shanghai from a place, visited the Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee on Renji Road yesterday and personally reported that near Haining, a family of seven, including the husband, wife, and children, had suffered from a drought and consumed all their food and pawned their belongings. They had been unable to cook for three days. A neighbor woman, unable to bear the sight, shared several liters of rice to provide immediate relief. However, when her husband returned, he said that this little amount was not enough even for their own needs, let alone sharing with others. What would their family live on? They quarreled, and the sound reached outside. The famine-stricken family heard this and returned the rice. Another neighbor, learning of the situation and seeing the husband and wife groaning in pain, generously lent them one dollar that had been saved in the tattered quilt, hoping to save their entire family. Unexpectedly, although the famine-stricken family had obtained this dollar, they felt that they could not survive in this environment. They were seized by a fleeting idea. They purchased two jiao of broken rice and eight jiao of sodium nitrate, cooked porridge, and all seven members of the family consumed it, resulting in their deaths. The tragedy filled the village, shocking everyone. Dr. Wang also stated that there were still 1,500 households in Haining that could be saved. The provincial relief funds were limited and could not provide timely assistance. Providing relief at a rate of 200 yuan per day would cost only 6,000 yuan for a month and could save a significant number of lives. It was said that the committee had been providing emergency relief to Haining and had repeatedly increased its funding, coordinating with the Jisheng Association to distribute the funds. It had just been completed, yet such a tragedy had occurred. This showed that the disaster was severe, and the relief funds were insufficient to provide a thorough solution. It was hoped that all sectors would quickly offer assistance, as the weather was cold and freezing, making this a timely and virtuous act.

Life is hanging by a thread. Moreover, how can they sow the seeds and have hope for spring plowing? The cries of the hungry are unbearable all day long. Those who have children can flee to other places, and these are the people who are able to survive. The dead are gone and cannot speak. At this time of extreme anxiety and before it is too late, people of society should save the money spent on Spring Festival banquets and use it for disaster relief. In this way, disaster victims will benefit greatly, and it is particularly hoped that charitable comrades will do this.

A Western Employee of Jardine Matheson Forces a Chinese Worker to Death, the National Seamen's Union Offers Support

Tian Hou, a Chinese worker in the middle cabin of the Xianghe Steamer of Jardine Matheson, missed the ship in Shanghai. He boarded the Longhe Steamer to pursue it to Beijing. He was forced to disembark at Xiaguan. By the time he got to Xiaguan, the Xianghe had already set sail. Therefore, he still boarded the Longhe Steamer going upstream. When the worker boarded the steamer in Shanghai, he originally paid 1 yuan and 1 jiao to purchase a half-price ticket. The second time he boarded the steamer from Beijing, he could not buy a ticket because he had no money. A Western ticket checker, Niumen, discovered this. Although Tian stated the reason, the Westerner not only did not show consideration to a fellow seamen in the same company, but also violently beat him and insulted him in every way, firmly demanding that he buy a ticket. Tian was forced to jump into the river to commit suicide. When all the passengers on the ship saw this, they were greatly angered and immediately ordered the captain to stop the ship and retrieve him, but he was already barely breathing. By the time they arrived at Wuhu, he had already died. An autopsy was performed in Wuhu. The results showed that Tian had drowned due to injuries sustained before death. This case has now aroused the indignation of seamen all over the country, who are determined to unite and provide assistance. A committee has been organized to handle the negotiations. The Chinese Seamen's Union has been receiving messages from seamen's organizations all over the country, stating that the facts of this case are not only about the abuse of Chinese workers, but also involve international indignation. They are currently conducting a detailed investigation and collecting evidence. Once the matter is settled, they will seriously lodge a protest.

That the Original Tax Should Not Be Increased

The Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Association has repeatedly received reports from its members, such as Wan Mao Xiang and other shops, that after they paid the tax for the Spring cigarette licenses, officials from the South Shanghai Tax Collection Office were sent to investigate and planned to levy an additional level of tax. Recently, tax officials have again visited their shops, instructing them to increase the rate for the spring quarter as well. Merchants are hoping to reduce their burdens and maintain their livelihoods during this time of sluggish market conditions and declining business. If the rate is increased again, they will be unable to afford it. If business can be developed, they will naturally comply with the order to increase the rate. Please ask the association to forward their plea to the Tax Bureau to grant them consideration and allow them to pay taxes at the original rate in order to maintain their livelihoods. A Japanese Steamer, the Hakushin Maru, Collides with a Coal Boat

The Boatmen's Association Submits a Request to the Maritime Affairs Bureau for Compensation

Barge No. 12169 of the Zhu Xianji Barge Company in this port, carrying 50 tons of Hongqi coal, was being towed by the Longxing tugboat at approximately 4:00 PM on January 15th, passing through the Dongjiadu Middle Pier on the Puxi side. At that time, the Hakushin Maru, a steamer belonging to the Dalian Steamship Company of Japan, was turning its head to exit the harbor, piloted by the Nanyang tugboat. The hull of the steamer was obstructing the center of the harbor. Suddenly, the steamer reversed. The stern of the steamer crashed into the Puxi side. The Longxing tugboat repeatedly sounded its whistle as a warning, but the Hakushin Maru continued to reverse. The steamer collided with the coal boat in the middle, causing the cargo and boat to sink completely, resulting in a huge loss. The owner of the barge, Zhu Xianrui, has reported this to the Coal and Stone Barge Industry Association of this city for assistance. The association, upon receiving the report, has submitted a request to the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation for filing. They will send personnel to inspect the damage and negotiate with the Dalian Steamship Company for compensation.

Buddhist Organizations Cast a Massive Bell for the Far East

Weighing 28,000 Catties and Made Entirely of Copper

The Model is Currently on Display at the Buddhist Laymen's Forest

The Buddhist Laymen's Forest of this port, the Municipal Buddhist Association, the Chinese Buddhist Association, the Buddhist Pure Land Society, the Buddhist Lotus Society, the Buddhist Bookstore, and six other organizations have initiated the casting of a massive bell weighing 28,000 catties and made of pure copper. It will be installed on the highest peak of Jiuhua Mountain. The height of the bell will be comparable to the eaves of a two-story house. The diameter of the bell mouth will be fourteen feet in both directions. After being installed on the high peak of Jiuhua Mountain, the sound of the bell will be audible for hundreds of miles. The bell is currently being cast by the Shen Yuanji Foundry in Pudong. A model of the bell, weighing forty catties and made of copper, has been made. The style is elegant and is now on display in the Buddhist Laymen's Forest on Xinmin Road, Zhabei.

Lu Xihou Returns to Prison

Whether There is a Relationship with the Jai Alai Stadium Needs to Be Investigated

The Civil Court Believes That There is a Need for Custody

Lu Xihou, Chairman of the China Industrial Bank, has been arrested since the bank collapsed. Lu Xihou was allowed to be released on bail of 20,000 yuan in cash and 30,000 yuan in bonds in order to go out and settle debts. However, when Lu was preparing the funds for bail the other day, because he had been subject to civil court liquidation, he accompanied lawyers Fan Gang and Wu Kun to the Civil Division Six for questioning. Judge Yu Changzi opened the court for trial and asked if Lu had invested in the jai alai stadium and the dog racing track. The debts he owed to others amounted to approximately 900,000 yuan, while others owed him over 1 million yuan. Although these were old accounts, he could still recover over 100,000 yuan. At the same time, there were 150,000 yuan in pledges from the Siming Bank, 150,000 yuan in advances from the Qunyi Banking Syndicate, and over 100,000 yuan in savings from relatives and friends. If the two were offset, he only owed about 500,000 yuan, so he planned to pay off half of it first, regardless of the size of the account. Black Fever Discovered in Jiangbei

The Seaport Quarantine Service Prevents Spread

The Ministry of Health Sends Personnel to Diagnose and Treat

The Dagong News Agency reports: Recently, the weather has been unfavorable, and various infectious diseases are prone to break out. Recently, cases of black fever have been discovered in the Jiangbei area of Jiangsu Province. There are a considerable number of patients. The National Seaport Quarantine Service is strictly preventing its spread, as it concerns public health. The details are as follows:

Wu Liande Discusses the State of the Disease

According to Mr. Wu Liande, director of the Quarantine Service, speaking to the Dagong News Agency reporter yesterday, the infectious disease discovered in the Jiangbei area of Jiangsu Province is black fever in medicine, known as Black Fever in English. The disease is caused by unhygienic condition. It starts with a slight fever, then the abdomen gradually becomes swollen, as large as a pregnant woman, similar to leprosy, and is extremely contagious. It is prevalent in tropical areas such as Burma and Annam. Cases have also been discovered in Shandong and other provinces in China, but it is not the black death disease reported in the newspaper. The Quarantine Service is strictly preventing its spread.

Set Up Clinics for Timely Treatment

The Jiangbei area is mostly rural, so most of those infected with black fever are farmers. The Ministry of Health believes that as an infectious disease, it should be eradicated as soon as possible. Therefore, it has sent Dr. Sun Zhirong of the Quarantine Service to set up clinics and actively treat the disease. It is hoped that it can be eradicated in the shortest possible time. Based on the current observation of the disease, it does not seem likely to spread excessively. Appropriate preventive measures have already been taken in this city.

The Tragic Story of a Blacklisted Young Woman

Drifting in Shanghai, Full of Regret

Dying in Poverty and Sickness in a Foreign Land

Cao Ada, a young woman from Kunshan, aged twenty-four, had a habit. She recently became addicted to smoking opium, which caused her to wander around. She was a sluggard all day long. She intensified and the habit was bigger than before. Wang reluctantly divorced her. This ignorant village woman was addicted to opium and was not tolerated in the family. After leaving the family, she was dissatisfied. She was wandering alone, living under a tower, and she lived a very disappointing life. She said to tell them that it was not a lie, because she was sick. She said for him to come quickly because she might not see him again. When she was done, she was in tears, regretting everything. Everyone was surrounding her, and they pitied her. But yesterday morning, someone was looking for Cao Ada and found her dead. It was found that the door was locked, and they notified the local court. They found Cao Ada, who was wearing torn clothes and covered in sores, and she was malnourished and dead. They sent the casket to be found by the family, and later someone was sent to find Cao Zaifeng in Kunshan. They hope that he will bury her.

Remainder of House Rented Out to Tenant Who Was a Robber

Happily Opened the Door to Move Belongings In

Pulled Out a Gun and Rummaged Through Chests and Cabinets

Zheng Shengquan, a Ningbo native, 47 years old, residing at No. 1 Jixin Fang, Lane 71, East Zilaihuo Street, in the French Concession, acted as a sub-landlord. He lived in the room behind the living room and rented out the remaining rooms upstairs. Recently, the tenant of the entire three-story building had moved out, so he posted a rental notice at the entrance of the lane. On the 16th in the morning, a man with a local accent came to Zheng's house to rent the room. He inspected the place once but did not commit to anything. However, he had already looked around upstairs and downstairs before leaving. On the 17th in the afternoon, the man came again to view the house. This time, he paid a deposit of one silver dollar, rented the room, and arranged to move in the next day. Yesterday at noon, the man came to Zheng's house again, claiming to be moving his belongings in, and requested the main door to be opened. Zheng's family, suspecting nothing, happily opened the door. Suddenly, three robbers, dressed in long black gowns and speaking in Chongming, Ningbo, and local accents, rushed in. They brandished three handguns, threatening the occupants not to make a sound. The man who had called for the door to be opened also joined the gang. Zheng and his family, seeing the guns, were afraid and dared not make a sound, allowing the robbers to ransack the rooms, rummage through chests and cabinets, and search Zheng himself. They were robbed of clothes, jewelry, and cash worth about 300 yuan in total. After obtaining the loot, the robbers fled. Afterward, the victim reported the loss to the French police station and requested an investigation. Upon receiving the report, the police chief dispatched detective Wu Lianrong to investigate the scene and ordered all detectives to strictly apprehend the robbers and bring them to justice.

Red Pill Trademark Also Had English Label Stating "Made in Germany"

A Factory Uncovered on Parker Road

Many People Involved, Hearing Postponed

Wu Hanzhang, a Chinese detective of the Narcotics Division of the General Police Station, recently detected that someone was running a red pill factory and secretly selling them at No. 88 Renxin Li, Lane 253, Parker Road. He sent an informant, disguised as a customer, to obtain a sample packet and inquire about the price. Each bag of 1,000 pills sold for $6.50. They agreed to meet the day before yesterday at 4:00 PM to pay $65 for ten bags of red pills, totaling 10,000 pills. The informant reported back to Detective Wu, who informed the First Special Court and obtained a search warrant. They secretly waited outside No. 88 Renxin Li the day before yesterday. At the same time, they sent the informant inside, pretending to buy, and contacted a woman named Xu Yangshi. She instructed him to call her mother, Xu Wushi, at 3247 (i.e., Yi Tai Yong Coal Store, No. 48 Pushi Road, French Concession) to have the goods delivered from the factory. Before long, a Ningbo man named Hu Jinsheng arrived carrying a coal basket. Just as he was about to enter, detectives arrested him outside the door. They found ten bags of red pills, weighing five and a half pounds, hidden in the coal. They then went inside, arrested the two women, and searched the premises but found no further contraband. Based on Hu's confession, they, together with detectives from the French police, went to Yi Tai Yong Coal Store and found 26 pounds of red pills, three taels of powder, two pounds of coffee extract, one red pill press, two baskets, and two cans of red pill dye on top of the firewood. Only a Ningbo woman named Zhang Wangshi was apprehended at the time. Later, Hu Jinsheng confessed that the red pills came from the Shidai Pharmacy at No. 21 Jinshou Li, Shandong Road. Chinese and Western detectives then went to Shidai Pharmacy and arrested Zhang Zinan, a Ningbo native, and his brother Zhang Ziqing (a doctor), who were accomplices. They found 16 pounds of raw materials, five bottles of resin (weighing five and a half pounds), and five cans of caffeic acid under the bed in the back room. All were taken to the police station and detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, presented the case and stated that the red pills seized had a "Double Lion Horse" trademark and were labeled with English letters stating that the goods were of high quality and made in Germany. He also learned that the person in charge was Liu Chongfa, the manager of Yi Tai Yong Coal Store, who was now on the run. He requested permission to detain the defendants and postpone the hearing. Judge Liu Yugui briefly questioned Xu Yangshi and the other six people. Their statements were mostly evasive. He ordered them to be detained for seven days for further questioning.

Zhang Guanghua Denies Killing His Younger Brother

Trial Opened Yesterday, Statements Taken

Further Investigation of the Case Is Necessary

Zhang Guanghua, a Henan native, 27 years old, formerly employed by the Shanghai Shipping Administration Bureau, and his 18-year-old younger brother, Zhang Guangzhou, lived together in a third-floor attic room at the home of a Ningbo woman, Dai Chenshi, at No. 24 Chongde Fang, Minguo Road, outside the Xiaobeimen in the French Concession. On November 22 of last year, Zhang Guanghua's employment was terminated, and he informed the sub-landlord that he would vacate the room in five or six days with his brother to return to Henan. That night, the two brothers still slept in the same room. At 5:00 AM the next morning, Zhang Guangzhou was suddenly killed by a knife that severed his neck. Zhang Guanghua also suffered five or six knife wounds to the head at the same time, jumped out of the window shouting for help, and then called to open the window of the attic room on the second floor, where a Haiyan native named Yan Jintao lived. The sub-landlord's relatives, Dan Bingchang and Lin Shengxiang, went out to call the police. The police sent Guanghua to the hospital for treatment and transported Guangzhou's body to the coroner for examination. Since there were no other relatives in Shanghai, the Charity Hall arranged for the burial. Later, after Guanghua recovered from his injuries, the police took him back for a thorough investigation and determined that Guangzhou had indeed been killed by Guanghua. They sent Guanghua to the Second Special Court and filed a public prosecution for murder. On the 8th of this month, Judge Xiong Huiping opened a trial and questioned witnesses Dai Chenshi, Yan Jintao, Dan Bingchang, Lin Shengxiang, and others. Instructions were given to postpone the trial for further investigation, as detailed in the newspaper on the 9th. During the postponement, the presiding judge, Mr. Xiong, personally went to the scene of the incident to survey and inquire about the circumstances at the time. Yesterday was the date for the continued hearing. Judge Xiong and Clerk Tao specially opened the Second Criminal Court for the trial. Lawyer Yuan Jiahuang from the Police Department appeared in court. The defendant, Zhang Guanghua, also hired a lawyer to defend him. The defendant's father, Zhang Wenfubu, also came to court to listen. According to Zhang Guanghua's statement, "Our brothers have always had a good relationship." Asked, "How could such a tragedy occur?" He replied, "After being injured, I escaped. I don't know. We turned off the lights at night to sleep. In my sleep, someone used a knife to stab my head. I woke up, got up, and couldn't open the door, so I opened the window and jumped out, shouting for help. This person then stabbed my younger brother." Asked, "Was it your younger brother who stabbed you?" He replied, "It was dark, so I couldn't see clearly. I was sleeping on the bed by the east window, with my feet facing the door. When I slept, my head was covered with a quilt, my right shoulder was down, and my left shoulder was up." At this point, the witnesses were questioned one by one. Their statements were the same as recorded in the previous report. The judge then said to the defendant, "It is now proven that there was no third person in your room. Based on various observations, it is presumed that your brother stabbed you, and you resisted in self-defense, which is reasonable. You also confessed this way when moving out." Zhang replied, "Our brothers have always been harmonious, and he was very obedient to me. If he had disobeyed me, I could have asked him to live elsewhere. How could I have harmed my own brother in this way?" At this point, the judge stated that the case still required detailed investigation and ordered the clerk to read aloud the written records of the statements of each person and sign them. He then announced that the hearing would be postponed to a later date, and the defendant would remain in custody.

Zhu Liqing Case Opened for Execution Yesterday

Le Songxiong Has Not Paid Alimony

The Court Will Schedule Another Summons

Zhu Liqing, a young woman from Nanjing, resided at No. 30 Datong Li, Yaozhujiao Road, in the French Concession. She had received a higher education and was well-versed in both Chinese and Western knowledge. In the spring of 1930, she was hired as an English teacher by Le Zhenbao, a Ningbo native who owned the Taichang Wood Shop on Nanjing Road. At that time, Le's son, Songxiong, was a comprador in the film department of the Pacific Trading Company. Seeing Zhu's talent and beauty, he could not help but desire her. He pursued Zhu in every possible way. In 1930, he invited Zhu to visit the scenic spots of Hangzhou, and they had an ambiguous relationship. In April of the following year, Zhu gave birth to a daughter, named Zhier by Songxiong. At the same time, Songxiong rented a house with Zhu at No. 598 Laoshenfu Road and lived together. In October of 1932, Zhu gave birth to another daughter, named Ren'er. After Zhu lived with Le, their relationship was extremely harmonious. She even celebrated that she would be settled for life. Unexpectedly, the good times did not last long. Since last fall, Le suddenly changed his attitude towards Zhu, treating her like an old fan. Zhu had no choice but to hire Lawyer Xue Jiaqi to file a complaint with the Civil Court of the Second Special Court, requesting that the defendant Le Songxiong be ordered to pay living expenses of $12,000 and return the advance payment of $1,500. Judge Ma Yishu of the court summoned the defendant Le Songxiong several times. Le Songxiong also hired Lawyer Yan Yinwu to represent him in court and filed a counterclaim, requesting that he be granted a divorce from Zhu, that the two daughters be handed over, and that Le be responsible for raising them. The case has already been judged, ordering the defendant Le Songxiong to pay the plaintiff Zhu Liqing alimony of $6,000 and return the advance payment. During the appeal period, he must pay monthly living expenses of $60. The defendant's lawsuit was rejected. However, the defendant has not paid to date. Yesterday morning was the date for civil execution. Judge Shu summoned both parties for execution. The living expenses for the two months during the appeal period, totaling $120, have not been paid. Only Zhu arrived in court. Judge Shu instructed that the defendant's summons had not been delivered and that another summons would be scheduled.

Since You Call Him Son-in-Law, There Is No Need to Abandon Amity and Exalt Enmity

Marriage Dispute Involves Litigation in Court

The Judge Believes Reconciliation Is Best

Gu Wenzhong, a local, is engaged in the customs brokerage business and lives on Zhonghua Road in the Nanshi district.

Welfare Agency Fills Out Interview Records for Vagrants

Zhang Zixin, the director of the Welfare Agency, sent a letter instructing the administrators to investigate the conditions of the poor and fill out interview records so that they could be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau. The letter stated, "Dear Sir, We have received a letter from the Social Affairs Bureau stating that the vagrant interview records have been printed by the Bureau. We are now sending 1,450 copies. Please fill them out in detail, item by item. If there are not enough, adults can be questioned and the records filled out. For those under the age of 16, another type of record can be used. A sample sheet is attached. Please print and handle accordingly." The vagrant interview records are handled by the Social Affairs Bureau for investigation and statistics purposes and have been handled in the past. We are now sending 500 copies and 100 copies of another sample sheet. We hope that you will follow the instructions, fill them out in detail, and submit them so that we can compile and forward them.

Vagrant Interview Record of the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau: What is your surname? What is your name? How old are you? Where are you from? Who are the members of your family? Where are they now? What are they doing? Can you read? Have you attended school? What skills do you have? How long have you been in Shanghai? How did you get here? What did you do when you first came to Shanghai? What do you do in Shanghai? How do you make a living? Have you ever sent money home while working in Shanghai? How often? Do you have any illnesses? When did you get into this situation? Why did you come here? Are you willing to change your situation? Why? Have you ever played mahjong? Do you gamble often recently? Do you drink alcohol? How much can you drink? What kind of alcohol? Do you have any cigarettes (opium, morphine)? Do you have any red pills? Among the prostitutes, can you name one or two? What is your relationship with them? Have you ever been involved in a lawsuit? What kind of case was it? Are you willing to correct your mistakes? How do you plan to correct them? After leaving the agency, where do you plan to go? What do you plan to do?

Last year, he formed an inextricable bond with Gu Yizhen, a woman from the countryside of Wuxi. Gu was only eighteen years old and unmarried. Her sister, Saizhen, lived in the Jiumu Di area of the city. After Gu had an affair with Yizhen, he initially promised to marry her. Therefore, Yizhen's mother, Bao, and Saizhen both agreed. Bao often addressed Gu as "son-in-law" in her letters and referred to herself as the mother-in-law. Letters were exchanged frequently, mostly through Saizhen, to avoid any mishaps. Unexpectedly, Gu Wenzhong recently became unfaithful and treated Yizhen as a stranger. Gu's mother, Bao, then, in her capacity as the legal guardian of her daughter, hired a lawyer to sue Gu Wenzhong for disrupting the family in the First Special District Court and requested that he be interrogated and punished according to law. Judge Wu Tingqi opened a hearing several times. It was learned that Gu Bao had already recognized Gu Wenzhong as her son-in-law. He instructed both parties to go out and reconcile, and that there was no need to abandon amity and exult enmity. However, although both parties respected the judge's intention to settle the matter, they were still unwilling to engage in frank negotiations and reach a settlement. Half a month has passed, and it has not been resolved. Yesterday afternoon, the hearing was scheduled to resume. The defendant Gu Wenzhong did not appear, but the plaintiff was represented by Gu Yizhen and her lawyer, who requested another postponement to continue negotiations. Judge Wu then granted the request and postponed the hearing to 2:30 PM on the 25th of next month. If a settlement is reached before the next hearing, then they may submit a statement requesting the withdrawal of the complaint.

The Zhabei Soup Kitchen Invites the Press for a Visit

The Zhabei Liuying Road Soup Kitchen invited members of the Shanghai press to visit the kitchen yesterday morning. At 8:00 AM yesterday morning, more than a dozen reporters from various newspapers gathered at the Guanshengyuan on Nanjing Road. After a light breakfast, they departed at 8:30 AM. They arrived at the Liuying Road kitchen at 9:00 AM. Then, led by Wang Binyan and others, they toured the facility. The tour concluded around 10:00 AM, and the kitchen provided transportation to take them back. Details are as follows:

More Than 20,000 People Crying Out for Food. When the reporters arrived at Liuying Road, the soup distribution had just ended. A mass of impoverished people, men, women, and children, in tattered clothes, carrying ladles and bowls, were crowding out of the soup kitchen. In this beautiful city, who could have imagined that there were so many refugees crying out for food? Roughly estimated, there were no fewer than 20,000 people, all with sorrowful faces, a truly heartbreaking sight. The reporters then got out of the car and were greeted by Mr. Wang Binyan and others, who invited them inside for a tour.

Those Who Did Not Get Soup Received Copper Coins. Inside, there were three crude bamboo sheds, built with dense bamboo grids for people to sit and rest. One was for men, one for women, and one for children. This was to prevent crowding during distribution and to protect women and children from being crushed. Therefore, each shed had its own separate entrance and exit. Security guards were stationed at the site to maintain order, which was relatively good. There were also five straw huts, each with two stoves, and each stove had three pots, with large vats placed beside them, totaling seventeen. Based on the soup distribution yesterday morning, a total of forty dan of rice were cooked. Those who were unable to receive soup were given copper coins instead, totaling fifty-three yuan. The cooking of the soup began at 11:00 PM and was stored in the vats. Each vat could feed 300 people. The doors opened at 4:00 AM, and people went to the soup distribution room to receive soup. Adults received three ladles each, and children received two ladles each. After receiving the soup, they went to the bamboo sheds. The doors closed around 8:00 AM and the distribution was completed around 9:00 AM. When the doors were closed, the bamboo sheds were opened, and people left in batches.

Wang Binyan Discussed the Plight of the Poor. Mr. Wang told the Central News Agency reporter that as many as 20,000 to 30,000 impoverished people from Zhabei and Jiangwan came here daily seeking food due to hunger and cold. More than 7,000 were men, two-thirds of whom were young and strong. These were mostly unemployed workers or laborers, as more and more factories in Zhabei were closing down, and the business situation was becoming increasingly dire. Even rickshaw pullers could not earn enough to eat. Furthermore, it is important to note that in previous years, most of those who came for soup were from Jiangbei or Anhui, with very few locals. Now, even from as far as Jiangwan, there are many locals who endure the wind and dew at 2:00 AM and trek long distances in the hope of getting a bowl of soup. Because of the large number of people, the soup kitchen has to distribute soup to everyone it sees. However, what one person receives cannot support the whole family. Therefore, the elderly, the young, the sick, and the weak have to be brought along. People in Shanghai and various charitable organizations know about the disasters in various provinces and call for relief efforts, but they do not realize that the plight of the lower classes in Shanghai is no less severe than that of the disaster victims in various provinces. This is a regret. I hope that the gentlemen of the press will publicize this in the newspapers so that all sectors can understand the truth and provide practical assistance.

Both Railways Collect Old Uniforms to Help Disaster Victims

Previously, the Railway Bureau, considering the severe drought in various provinces last year and the widespread devastation among the disaster victims, decided to collect all the old uniforms stored in various offices in accordance with the spirit of mutual assistance, so as to help with relief efforts. Recently, the following items have been collected: 696 winter uniforms, 452 pairs of winter trousers, 98 coats, 12 summer uniforms, and 34 pairs of summer trousers. On January 15, a letter was sent to the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Relief of Drought Disasters in Various Provinces, requesting that it distribute the items on its behalf. Subsequent receipts will be sent in batches for redistribution.

The Bar Association Sends a Letter to the Court Requesting the Maintenance of Order

Issued Because of Ke Yinghao Assaulting Lawyer Zhu Si-fu

Regarding the case of Ke Yinghao, a Fujianese, relying on his Japanese nationality, arbitrarily yelling in the First Special District Court, the Shanghai Bar Association sent a letter to President Guo yesterday, requesting a correction. The original letter is recorded below: "Dear Sir, According to reports in the newspapers on the 12th of this month, Ke Yinghao, relying on his Japanese nationality, arbitrarily yelled in your court, disrespecting his superiors, and assaulting the opposing lawyer, Zhu Sifu, in court. This is outrageous. The dignity of the judiciary and the order of the court should be obeyed not only by the people of this country but also by foreigners of all countries. This Ke Yinghao, regardless of whether he is of Japanese nationality, arbitrarily destroys the order of the Chinese court. This is unacceptable to our judicial community. We hereby send this letter, hoping that your court will maintain the dignity of the court and legally stop Ke Yinghao when he is summoned again. If he engages in any illegal actions again, correct them immediately. "

Record of the Joint Meeting of the Rent Reduction Association

The Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee held its 35th joint meeting of the Legal, Design, and Execution Committees yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. Those in attendance included Wang Xianggu, Chen Jiufeng, Wang Jingdong, Zhang Xianfang, Chen Binghui, Zhu Zhichun, Liu Zhongying, Hu Fengxiang, Qiu Liangyu, Zhang Yumen, Ren Nongxuan, Zheng Xiaolin, Wei Langxuan, and more than 30 others. Zhang Xianfang chaired the meeting. After reporting on letters received from various parties, they discussed the following cases: (1) The Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions' proposal for three measures to relieve the city's economy. It was resolved that the proposal be unanimously supported and that a letter be sent to each district branch to follow it. (2) The proposal that the association send representatives to participate in the general assembly of industrial and commercial organizations. It was resolved to support Wang Xianggu, Wu Quan, and Zheng Xiaolin to participate. (3) The proposal that representatives be sent to Beijing to request the Executive Yuan and other agencies to issue a clear order to reduce rent in order to save the city's appearance. It was resolved to support Zhang Xianfang, Chen Jiufeng, Wang Xianggu, Zhu Zhichun, and Hu Fengxiang. The date was to be determined by the representatives. (4) The proposal to notify each district branch that rents should be deposited in banks before the rent reduction issue is resolved. It was resolved to pass it. (5) The proposal to send representatives to the Shanghai Municipal Government's Public Works Department to request that empty houses throughout the city be taxed minimally, starting from January 1. It was resolved that Chen Binghui, Liu Zhongying, Zhang Xianfang, and Wang Jingdong would be responsible for carrying it out. (6) The Pingquan Villa Branch of Meibaige Road requested registration. It was resolved to send a letter to register with the association in accordance with the law. (7) The proposal to expand the rent reduction movement to promote social attention. It was resolved to hand it over to a special committee to convene a general assembly of representatives from each district branch to discuss the method. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Pukou Station Issues Round-Trip Sightseeing Tickets for Both Railways

To Be Implemented Starting February 1st

Regarding the issuance of round-trip sightseeing tickets from Pukou Station on the Jinpu Railway to various stations on the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railways through the Shanghai-Pinglian Through Transport, the 17th National Joint Transport Meeting decided and the Ministry of Railways approved the measure. The sightseeing locations and validity periods of the round-trip sightseeing tickets will be handled in accordance with the methods of Nanjing Station on the Jinghu Railway. The Traffic Department of the Railway Bureau subsequently received a notice from the Traffic Department of the Jinpu Railway, stating that Pukou Station would start selling round-trip sightseeing tickets to Hangzhou, Chang'an, Xiashi, Jiaxing, Jiashan, Songjiang, Shangbei, Qingyanggang, Kunshan, Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou, Danyang, Zhenjiang, and Qixia Mountain starting on February 1 of this year. Blank round-trip sightseeing tickets would be used temporarily. The validity period was set at ten days for Pukou and Hangzhou and seven days for the other stations. The department had already notified all relevant sections and stations.

Case of Goods Falling and Crushing a Person to Death

Yu Qiaqing Grants Bereaved Family 500 Yuan in Compensation

Comprador Fan Generously Donates Money to Transport Coffin Back to Tianjin

On December 28 of last year, Huang Xiufeng, a Tianjin native, traveled from Tianjin to Shanghai on the Sanbei Company's Jing'an ship to look for his son. When the ship passed through the Black Water Ocean, the corn cargo in the cabin suddenly collapsed, crushing Huang to death. Huang's wife, Huang Anshi, upon hearing the news, came specially from Tianjin, grieving loudly over the coffin. Since Huang's tragic death had left nine family members without a livelihood and the eldest son was still studying, the second son was young, and the four daughters were all unmarried, in order to maintain their future livelihoods, she, along with her eldest son, Guisheng, went to the Sanbei Company on Guangdong Road to see General Manager Yu Qiaqing, personally explaining their plight and requesting compensation. Huang Guisheng also reported to the Eighth District Branch of the Second Special District City Federation of Trade Unions for assistance. The meeting decided to report it to the Second Special District City General Federation of Trade Unions. The meeting then decided to send a letter to Yu Qiaqing requesting generous compensation. Director Wu Guowei delivered the letter in person. Director Wu met with Yu Qiaqing in person and gently explained on behalf of the deceased's family. Yu Qiaqing was deeply sympathetic and agreed to grant a special condolence payment of 500 yuan. At the same time, Mr. Fan Menglin, the comprador of the Jing'an ship, also acted bravely out of a sense of justice and generously donated money to the deceased's family to transport Huang Xiufeng's coffin back to Tianjin, so as to avoid additional burden on the deceased's family. Huang Anshi and her son were deeply grateful. Therefore, they scheduled to submit a statement to the Procuratorate of the District Court in the morning, collect the coffin and close the case, and transport the coffin, go to the Sanbei Company to collect the condolence payment, and return to Tianjin on the same day.

If you are interested, please visit Mr. Gu at the office on the third floor of the Guanshengyuan Company on Nanjing Road to discuss.

A Minor Worker's Theft of Rice Causes a Disturbance

Yesterday at the Jardine Matheson & Co. wharf at Lujiazui, Pudong, the "Zhaoxing" steamship arrived. At 11:00 AM, while unloading rice, a porter named Ma Keli from Shandong secretly stole loose rice, concealing it around his waist, intending to leave the wharf. Li Buyue, a police officer stationed at the wharf, stepped forward to search him. Unexpectedly, Ma immediately dumped the stolen rice into the river, claiming the stolen goods were not found on him, and acting righteous and confident. Consequently, he argued with Officer Li. The officer then blew his whistle, summoning help from neighboring posts, who assisted in detaining Ma and taking him to the station for questioning. After a while, another porter, Zhang Xueyin, gathered dozens of fellow workers who swarmed the station entrance, demanding Ma's release. The workers were all armed with carrying poles, iron hooks, and other implements. As their demands were not met, they took the opportunity to smash the station's doors and window glass, and struck Officer Li Buyue, who was detaining Ma, causing skin injuries to his left hand and left side of his face. Another officer, Kong Xiangxi, also sustained a bleeding injury to the back of his left hand. They also tore the pocket of his uniform. Zhang Baiyi, the comprador of the wharf, learned of the incident and immediately notified the Pudong Public Security Bureau by telephone. Director Zhang of the bureau ordered Chief Guo Yongliang to lead officers to suppress the disturbance, which fortunately did not escalate. The instigating workers, Ma Chongli, Zhang Xueyin, and foreman Wei Rixin, were taken to the bureau for interrogation. The two injured officers were sent to Pudong Hospital for treatment. At this point, the Shandong workers collectively ceased work in a show of support. The bureau then dispatched officers a second time to suppress the unrest, and the workers resumed their work. Afterward, the bureau chief transferred the three apprehended individuals to the main bureau for further action. In the afternoon, the comprador of the wharf sent a letter to the bureau, detailing that the workers had been previously disputing over unsuccessful attempts to increase wages for the upstairs and downstairs loading work for the second and third floors of the warehouse, and that they used this incident as a pretext to cause trouble, requesting continued police protection to prevent a strike, etc.

Worker Injured in House Demolition

Two buildings at No. 46 and No. 48 Xinxing Road, west of the Han Bridge in Zhabei, had previously suffered a major fire. Although there was no significant loss, the wooden beams, bricks, and tiles were no longer usable. Therefore, the landlord hired a construction company to demolish them for reconstruction. Yesterday at around 3:00 PM, six or seven workers were climbing on the roof, removing the roof tiles when the roof beams, having become charred and brittle after the fire, could not withstand the load and broke, causing all the workers to fall. Fortunately, the height was not great, and they only suffered minor injuries. An ambulance was summoned and they were taken to the Second Hospital of the Red Cross for treatment.

Gambling Case at Hong Yun Restaurant Adjudicated

The Hong Yun Restaurant in the French Concession, on the Caishi Road, had recently rented its main hall to the gambling boss Shao Youfeng, ostensibly for a birthday celebration, to gather people for gambling and profiting from commissions. This was discovered by detectives Hang Bingquan, Bao Zongyu, and Cai Zongyi of the French Concession Police's gambling squad. They immediately rushed there and arrested the boss Shao Youfeng, Zhou Jinsheng, and 88 gamblers, including Zhou Guangyuan, Hu Siming, Gao Guanghou, Cheng Yifei, Shao Si, Hu Guisong, Zhou Afu, etc. They confiscated four sets of mahjong tiles, one set of pai gow tiles, two decks of playing cards, and over one hundred yuan in gambling money. On the grounds that the restaurant provided a gambling venue in violation of regulations, the manager Zhou Yanzhe and others were arrested and taken to the Second Special Court for prosecution. Judge Sun Pengxian of the Eighth Criminal Court presided over the trial. He ordered Shao Youfeng and Zhou Yanzhe to be detained, and the others were released on bail pending sentencing. As noted in previous reports, yesterday, Judge Sun sentenced boss Shao Youfeng for gathering people for gambling to a fine of 200 yuan, Zhao Yanzhe for violating regulations to a fine of 150 yuan, the waiter Zhou Jinsheng to a fine of 10 yuan, and the other gamblers to fines of 5 yuan, 3 yuan, and some were declared not guilty. The gambling implements and gambling money were confiscated according to the list.

Two New Rubbings Recently Published by the Medical Bookstore

Rubbing of Lv Yaoxian's Xiao Jian Four-Zhu coin, one volume. This is a rubbing of the Xiao Jian Four-Zhu coin, presented by Vice Minister Lv Yaoxian to Mr. Chen Shouqing. There are as many as fifty-four kinds. Bao Zinian's "Spring Said" says, "The Xiao Jian Four-Zhu has the character 'Ye' on one side and the character 'Xiao' on one side, which is the most difficult to obtain. The so-called one coin in the capital costs two to three thousand coins. At the end of the Daoguang period, an urn was suddenly unearthed in Southern China. Yaoxian collected hundreds of them and distributed them to others. Not only are they of different sizes, but some are upside down on one side, some are read from left to right, and there are also differences between one character being upright and one character being upside down. Some are placed horizontally on one side, above and below the perforation, and some are facing left and right. Some are upside down on one side, and some are shaped on one side, or both sides are shaped, and there are four stars, four circles, and four broken patterns. The Xiao Jian has the difference between the same text or upside down horizontal placement on both sides, and the Four-Zhu also has the same text on both sides, and the Four-Zhu characters are also made above and below the perforation. There are as many as fifty-four kinds of peculiarities. Although it is as small as an elm pod, it is green and refreshing, and it is absolutely worthy of treasure. Coinage coins are becoming more and more strange, and they are fully prepared in our dynasty. I believe that the earth does not love treasure." Now, comparing Bao's theory with this rubbing, there is no disagreement. It is truly a grand view of the Xiao Jian Four-Zhu coin. Now, it is printed with a glass plate, which is exactly the same as the true rubbing. The actual price is one yuan per volume.

Rubbing of Chen Shouqing's Six Coin Ten Bu coin, one volume. This is a rubbing presented by Mr. Chen Shouqing to Vice Minister Wu Qingqing. First, Wang Mang's Yang Quan Ten Bu is listed. Ten Bu has two pairs, one with a small straight line above the perforation, and the other without it. At the end, rubbings of ancient coins such as Libu are attached. Now, Chen's original version is printed, which is exactly the same as the true rubbing. Seeing it is like seeing the true coin. The actual price is one yuan per volume. General distributor: Yiyao Bookstore, No. 204 Mei Baige Road, Shanghai.

Organization of the Fruit Trade Union Association

All fruit store employees, in view of the fact that in recent years they have been subjected to pressure from the capital side, using the sweat and blood of their lives like cows and horses to exchange for meager wages, repeatedly suffering deductions by the store owners, and in order to increase the knowledge and skills of the employees, improve their lives, etc., it is particularly necessary to organize a group. Therefore, dozens of employees initiated it and jointly submitted a request to the Municipal Party Department, requesting the organization of the Shanghai Fruit Industry Occupational Union, which was approved. Nine people, including Rong Baokang, Hong Dexing, Shen Baokun, Xu Binggui, Bao Liren, Chu Songhai, Weng Wuquan, Jiang Wenquan, and Zheng Wensong, were appointed as preparatory members. When registration began, Cai Runshen, chairman of the Fruit Land Trade Association, repeatedly ordered the employees to sign letters of intent and guarantees, etc., based on the provisions of Articles 31 and 32 of the Trade Union Law, in order to destroy the organization, almost causing a major dispute. After mediation, in order to settle the matter, the labor side followed the mediator's intention and changed the name of the Shanghai Fruit Industry Occupational Union to the Shanghai Fruit Industry Employee Association, which was still approved by the Municipal Party Department. After discussion at a meeting of the employees, it was decided that Rong Baokang and the other nine people would continue to be responsible for the preparations. It is heard that the association is preparing to hold a general meeting to elect directors and supervisors in due course, so that its success can be observed.

Special Article

Peng Xiangying's Lecture on the Relationship Between Citizens and Air Defense (Continued)

However, at this time when we should work hard, we must fully prepare the sand and fire extinguishers used to extinguish fires caused by incendiary bombs, and the buckets of water and other items used for fire prevention. Within the realm of possibility, we must also purchase gas masks, so that when enemy planes drop both incendiary bombs and gas bombs during wartime, we can engage in firefighting work.

However, in wartime, if an incendiary bomb falls, it must be immediately covered with sand and extinguished to prevent it from spreading. If it has spread and spread to other objects, fire extinguishers or buckets of water should be used to extinguish it. Even residents in neighboring lanes must immediately gather and cooperate to carry out rescue. In addition, government offices, schools, factories, and major companies should always have fire-fighting equipment, and organize staff, workers, and students into fire brigades for pre-training. Then, with wartime preparations, if peacetime disasters occur, fire-fighting benefits can be obtained more effectively.

The above is specifically about the fire-fighting item. The responsibilities borne by citizens are so important. During air raids, all tasks such as anti-virus, rescue, engineering, security, traffic management, and alarm transmission also need to be mainly undertaken by citizens, because these are the affairs that are most closely related to citizens. If citizens do not automatically take on these tasks, even if the government leads them, it is not easy to achieve thorough and widespread results. Therefore, the relationship between citizens and air defense is indeed very close, and the task of air defense is indeed entirely up to the citizens.

Recently, our government authorities have felt that the national crisis is frequent, and the crisis is imminent. The ambitions of strong neighbors are on the rise. If something happens one day, our important cities will inevitably be attacked by air in an instant and reduced to ashes. Therefore, in November of last year, the first large-scale air defense exercise was held in the capital. This can be said to be a creation in the national air defense facilities, because this air defense exercise not only gave the citizens of Nanjing a very deep understanding of air defense, but also made the people of the whole country aware of the need for air defense. If we have a considerable understanding of air defense and know that it is an urgent and serious problem, we should actively study it and work hard to implement it. Although our country lacks financial resources and is behind in everything, the necessary national defense construction cannot be achieved in a moment. But as long as all our comrades can be determined to work hard, it will not be difficult to catch up and keep pace with the great powers. (End)
