Free Talk

Art and Beauty

— Ms. Zhou Manya

Goethe said, "Art is but a lending of form." We can change this definition and say, "Art is a method of expression or presentation." Then this question arises: if art is a method of lending form or expressing presentation, then what does it give in order to express form? We can answer this: art gives "human consciousness" (Humanconscjousness) to express and present, and reveals human thoughts and feelings. Regardless of the field of art, pure and joyful communication, full expression of life, and beautiful presentation of form, in the creation of all beautiful images and pleasant sounds, is the initial and original function of art.

"Creating thoughts" and "revealing emotions" and giving them form, or finding the appropriate method of expression, is the subjective spiritual task of all art. In order to achieve this goal, there is a need for objective mediums, and in accordance with the criteria of all beautiful entities of this medium, "the wheels of art" (ThevihicIeufart), concretely speaking, are "writing," "tone," and all "stiff materials." The skilled driving of these wheels, and a deep understanding of their beautiful qualities, is the important task of the artist. Whether the experience is profound and the skills are adept can distinguish the degree of success of artists with the same thoughts and feelings.

But we must understand that the artist, in order to express a thought or emotion, creates a certain model, which is not his ultimate goal. This form is merely a cumulative expression of oneself after a spiritual satisfaction. Similarly, the "pursuit of beauty" is not the ultimate goal of art, but merely an indispensable creation in the artistic expression caused by spiritual satisfaction! The task of art is to create an ideal world. All consciousness, emotions, tacit understandings, and qualities of life caused by thoughts are expressed in beautiful concrete forms. From this, we can know that the logical criticism of art requires us not only to measure an artist's technical ability and his expression of the qualities of beauty in the elements of artistic consciousness, but to go a step further and ask which part of the human spirit this artist has chosen to express in the form of creation. However, the thoughts contained in a work are not necessarily created by art, because human emotions and thoughts are often shared due to racial or conscious connections. For example, the concept of "divine sovereignty" expressed in "OIyumpiaZeusofpheidies", or the "great maternal love" expressed in Raphael's "ModomadiSanSisto", are mostly contemporary thoughts shared by the intellectuals. However, the artist's personality, his intellectual and moral characteristics, and the special path of his sensibility and thoughts, his personal attitude towards the materials that give him the concepts of expressing human consciousness, can all affect his choice of subject matter and the lending of form, and can determine the special form of the "beautiful model" he creates. For example, there are thoughts that are shared by the same race and era, giving the artist experience, and giving him experience is the decisive condition for the creation of artistic works, but his characteristics and the quality of his skills determine the success or failure of his works. What SignoIeei failed to achieve, Perugino succeeded and surpassed. Michelangelo is a profound writer, while Raphael is said to be the incarnation of beauty.

From this perspective, art is the artist's display of the analysis or expression of humanity to the masses. The subject matter of art contains everything that humans imagine, feel, sense, and do. Its depth is like religion, and its breadth is like life. But the difference between art and religion and life is that in works of art, the quality of beauty is attached. Without the quality of beauty, it cannot be established as something called art. The world of art is not a church or a school, but a wandering garden, a paradise on earth. He does not preach or preach to you clearly, but secretly and silently allows you to taste and contemplate. In the pastoral world of art, there is actually no mysterious or abstract thing, but some ordinary human things. "Truth" and "goodness" are transformed into "the quality of beauty" and manifest themselves in the world of art. Scientific and mechanical laws are not allowed to exist in the world of art. The world of art is a free world, in addition to the lively expression of humanity, it also gives mankind spiritual comfort and purity.

Memories of Wandering in Guandong

— Zang Kejia

Two days before the Dragon Boat Festival, I left the newly married Shen Ting, who was only twenty-seven days old, and wandered to Guanwai under an assumed name. The first stop was in Shenyang, lodging at the home of an old tenant farmer. They worked in a machine room there. A large earthen bed, long and narrow, was where both men and women slept. Besides the owners, there were several other villagers boarding there. They all made a living by selling vegetables. At first, I was not used to this life, but after a while, I could not help but get used to it. I did not tell them the truth. But I knew that they had question marks in their hearts about my movements. During the day, they went to sell vegetables and did not let me follow. I had to stay at home and chat with the old woman. Sometimes, unable to bear the boredom, I ran to the eastern suburbs to find my friends who sold vegetables. They seemed very worried about me and put a reed hat on my head, as if this could cover everything up.

I was waiting here for my grandfather's letter. The letter finally arrived, sewn onto the hem of a special messenger. My grandfather said that the matter was an iron case. Hope was like the sunlight that could not penetrate the dark clouds. He ordered me not to write home for ten years and told me not to act like a child crying for home. But I really cried like a child. I borrowed a pencil from a girl studying in a primary school through the bamboo fence and secretly wrote a letter home, putting a fake name on it and timidly dropping it into the mailbox.

A letter from my grandfather sent me thousands of miles away again. I transferred to Yilan on the banks of the Songhua River. Using a set of half-true, half-false words, I deceived a clan uncle from the same village and stayed with him. He was a clerk in the court, and his family was there too. The housing was too cramped, so he arranged for me to stay at the shop of an old Shandong fellow who sold noodles, two miles away. I asked my uncle to find me a job, so he ordered me to practice writing every day, as if the job would be in hand as soon as my writing was good. It often rained in Yilan, and after the rain, the mud on the ground was half a foot deep. Braving the rain and stepping through the mud, I spent the whole day struggling for food and lodging. On the way, I passed some dilapidated brothels, and some people, not knowing my suffering, leaned on the door and smiled at me.

My uncle finally introduced me to the court as a recorder. The department head gave a note, and the living expenses were fifteen yuan per month (Harbin dollars, equivalent to nine present dollars). Several colleagues congratulated me, saying that it was very promising to be approved for fifteen yuan together. They had been in the job for three years, and each of them received six dollars a month. I slept in the same room with a chief clerk. That person was stubborn but also an extreme hedonist, and his dumplings were filled with nine kinds of fillings. He drank all day and night, and when he was drunk, he cursed people.

When I first arrived in the department, everyone was nice to me, and the workers were also amiable. Later, it all changed. Important official documents were all pushed to me to write. I wrote carefully, but the more careful I was, the more mistakes I made. Every day, I wrote the names of criminals (to this day, I can still remember some long names of White Russian criminals) and heard the sound of shackles.

Three yuan were paid out for the Mid-Autumn Festival. After sending gifts to the department head, I had two yuan left. By this time, it had already snowed, and I was still wearing a lined coat. I bought some festival gifts with the money, braved the cold wind, and sent them to my uncle's house, telling everyone I met, "My uncle invited my family to celebrate the festival."

Young people and young people easily get close. I met a primary school principal, and in less than a week, I became his teacher. Half of my day was spent in the youth team, and life became a little more interesting. But in less than half a month, a letter from my grandfather suddenly brought unexpected joy and money. He told me to go to Shanghai immediately. After reading the letter, in half a day, I resigned from my part-time job, took out the money, sent a telegram to Shen Ting, and rushed to the ship. The principal was very surprised and sent someone to deliver a package of gifts to the ship, with a note attached, with very emotional words written on it, with my assumed name written on the top. As the ship sailed, I suddenly felt a little reluctant about the eight months of my life in Guanwai.

Rural Education

— Xu Ying

丨 "Continue with One Son and One Daughter"

When the stars in the sky squeezed their eyes, and the evening breeze coolly brushed my face, I found myself alone again at the head of the Little Clear River bridge. The Little Clear River's waters reflected the paper lanterns on the centipede boats, faintly trembling with threads of light in the darkness, spreading out into the black expanse. Suddenly, water splashed from the bow of a boat, with a "splash" sound, causing the hens to cluck in fright.

There were no pedestrians on this thoroughfare, and the noise temporarily died with the darkness. I mechanically passed this way every day. When there was a moon, a shadow always accompanied me, but now, I had even lost my shadow. Fortunately, I knew the way well. More than a year had passed, making my feet familiar with the ruggedness of the yellow mud road. I was especially pleased that the dog, barking wildly in the darkness, seemed familiar with my scent and trotted past me silently. I could even hear his faint panting.

Although I lived in the school converted from a small temple, I still had to go to the west of the river to tutor the son of Squire Zou in classical texts. A rural school teacher was not as good as the curly-haired dog guarding Squire Zou's gate. That dog fulfilled its duty and had other obligations. But me? Besides teaching children and adults, I also had to work as a free tutor. Every season, when I received the salary Squire Zou deducted from the school land, I had to offer a thousand thanks and ten thousand gratitudes.

I dragged my heavy steps, the rhythm of my heart corresponding with the rhythm of my steps. The sound of water from the bow startled me slightly, and I walked onto the bridgehead.

At this moment, my eyes twitched in the darkness. It seemed as if in the middle of the water, there was a pair of corpses, rising and sinking, as they had under the sun. I could not forget the relationship between these two people and me, but at the same time, I was curious as to why the two people were tied together as if they had committed adultery. For example, today's event was truly beyond my expectations.

The night wind brushed my face with a slight chill, and I smelled the garlic stench from my mouth.

The pungent garlic smell made me think even more deeply of the man bloated in the water, the man with a scar on his head. He gave me the ability to eat garlic. It was during the second semester of my night school. The scarred man was still my student. Seeing me tormented by stomach problems, he forced me to eat garlic every day. I had no choice but to try it. When I no longer felt nauseous at the sight of garlic stains on other people's yellow teeth, my stomach problems could be said to be mostly cured. ······

After hurrying along for about a mile, I saw the light from my little temple. In the lightless environment, the kerosene lamp seemed very bright. I didn't see any late students on the road. I was very happy, thinking of them anxiously waiting in the classroom, and I quickened my pace.

I walked into the main hall of the small temple, and a burst of carbon dioxide immediately surrounded me. The bodies of the crowd emanated fertilizer odors, and their breath reeked of pickled vegetables, overpowering my garlic smell. They were gathered in groups of three or five, chatting idly, buzzing like a swarm of bees. Seeing me enter, they successively returned to their seats. Black hands unfolded earth-colored books. Although I was holding a primer in my hand, my heart was still recalling the scarred floating corpse. My mouth unconsciously began to introduce a story to our university students.

"I will first tell you a story," I said. "This eldest brother is called" a good student. This student is as old as you are. Some of you could be his older brother, some could be his uncle. He had never studied before, and he didn't want to study, but later he did business, buying yarn in the city in bulk and selling it to the villagers to weave homespun cloth ·········"

They all understood what I was saying. Although the hand-cranked spinning wheels in these villages were not as numerous as those upstream, they all had looms to weave cloth, and recently, their yarn was bought from outside, with foreign letters printed on it.

"After he did business, he hated himself for not being able to write accounts, but there was no place to learn. Just at this time, I came to their village to teach students, pulling students everywhere, bowing and begging them to come and learn to read, but no matter what, I couldn't get a class together······"

Some students laughed at this, as some of them had been brought in by my bowing and begging. For example, Liu Huzi, who is yawning right now.

"But there were still no students. At this time, this student understood and came to me, saying that the villagers were holding golden bowls and begging for food, not knowing how to take advantage. I'll help you. I'll tell them to come and study. Those who don't come to study will have to pay me an extra string of cash when buying my yarn······ This way, the school over there was established. Do you think this student of mine is good? We must remember: it is not enough to only make yourself good, one must help others to be good together, that is truly good······ Okay, let's read!"

For farmers, it is enough to tell simple stories like this to make them understand. Saying a little about the good deeds of the scarred man who helped me, I felt a little comforted. I planned to tell people about the woman tied together at an appropriate opportunity.

Educational books, I am looking for an opportunity.

The Human World (4)

— Li Huiying

After he said this, his face still held a smile, but I could clearly see that the hostess's smile had completely disappeared, and it could be said that it was very sudden. Her face looked even paler. I was hesitating, unable to guess what this was, when my introducer spoke again:

"Are you afraid? What are you afraid of? I'll take care of it. You won't offend Director Li."

My friend saw the reason for the hostess's change of expression, explaining her doubts, her face was pale because of this, because she was engaging in private business, and I was a public official.

But how could I be a certain section chief of the "Manchukuo Puppet State" Harbin Police Department? Why was my friend lying to her? Why did he introduce me like this? Now, making the hostess fearful and uneasy, it really was my fault, and it seems that this responsibility should be borne by me. Therefore, I immediately explained to her:

"No, I'm not from the Police Department. Mr. Cao is joking, don't you know his character? You can rest assured."

I explained this way, fully believing that I could dispel her doubts, but seeing her face, which had not smiled for a long time, I knew that it had no effect at all. However, she seemed to have made up her mind not to care about this matter anymore. I could say that she wanted to suppress this matter and not talk about it. Therefore, she did not answer my words, but said something else:

"Xiaoju, pour tea. Please sit down, Director Li, Mr. Cao, I have really neglected you this time."

Xiaoju was the one who opened the screen for us, or the one who lit the lamp. I initially thought she was a thirteen-year-old girl, but this time, waiting for her to bring the tea from the east room, I looked more closely and saw that she was at least seventeen years old. She had a face of a suitable size, neither ugly nor dark. Her body was delicate, but she was a little short. She put down the tea set, took a few steps, tilted half of her body, and said to me with a smile:

"Director Li, I hope you can help my mother."

I nodded.

My doing this made it seem like I really was a director of the Police Department, like I could really help them, or, to put it bluntly, not make trouble for them. I couldn't help but smile inwardly.

However, saying that the hostess was her mother was a bit intriguing. A mother is only eight or nine years older than her daughter, unless she is a stepmother. Then, their titles were based on their status as prostitutes, right?

The hostess lit two opium lamps, inviting the two of us to smoke. I declined, in order to avoid trouble. I simply said that I was, in order to avoid

Reasonable."

"Director Li, you are too polite. Are you afraid of disturbing you in the future?"

The hostess strongly urged me, and from the looks of it, it seemed like she thought I said "reasonable" was deliberately making things difficult for her.

She came to pull me, smiling, and I was a little embarrassed, my face flushed for a while. In normal times, I rarely had young women staying over.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

Puyi Critically Ill

— Unable

"The other day, news from outside the Pass said that Puyi was critically ill, and the puppet organization was planning a grand ceremony committee to discuss the issue of succession to the throne. Yesterday, news came again that Puyi's condition had not improved, and treatments had been ineffective. Puyi has decided to go to Lushun for recuperation on the 21st of this month. The grand ceremony committee has been organized by Shen Ruilin, the puppet government's minister of the interior."

According to this news, Puyi's illness is feared to be incurable. But what exactly is his illness? Is it a mental illness or a physical illness? Puyi has been a puppet emperor of Manchukuo for just over a year, and now he is suddenly ill. Could it be that he doesn't even have the fortune to be a fake emperor? Or is he suffering from a critical political illness, making him incurable?

It is said that Puyi is still mentally clear. He became a Japanese puppet out of necessity and because he was surrounded by a group of sycophants like Zheng Xiaoxu. Since taking the stage, all his actions have been restricted, and he has been monitored by the Japanese in every way. He has said a few angry words, "Others say I am a puppet, but I am not even as good as a puppet. I am like a prisoner awaiting execution." This tone naturally indicates dissatisfaction with the Japanese who are directing and manipulating him. The Japanese political spies, who are densely deployed, must know the origin of Puyi's illness, which may lie in this.

Also, the other day, news came that the traitor Zhao Xinbo had returned from Japan after investigating constitutional government and had been shot by Lingjia under the pretext of hosting a banquet. It was said that the reason for his death was that Zhao mistakenly believed the puppet organization to be a genuine country. Therefore, he criticized the Manchus in the puppet organization for serving the Japanese in everything, and was shot by the Japanese authorities. Yesterday, news came from outside the Pass again that Zhao Xinbo had not been shot, but it was learned that Zhao was now recuperating at 7 Minamicho, Shibada Ward, Tokyo, under strict Japanese surveillance. It was said that Zhao's illness was a mental disorder and he was on the verge of death. Thus, even if Zhao was not shot, his mental state was abnormal under strict Japanese surveillance, and his death would not be far off.

Therefore, Puyi's illness and Zhao Xinbo's illness are both caused by the same type of political bacteria, so no matter what doctor is consulted, there is no way to treat them. Otherwise, the news of Puyi's serious illness has been announced outside the Pass for many days, but he has not died yet. Then whether he is sick is questionable. Even if he is sick, he can go to Lushun for recuperation, which may not be very serious. Why is the Japanese side urgently organizing a grand ceremony committee to discuss the issue of succession to the throne? By closely observing these various symptoms, the cause of Puyi's illness can be understood without saying it.

Therefore, I expect that there are many traitors in general who have this disease. However, because of the illnesses of Puyi and Zhao Xinbo, the other illnesses are suppressed by violence, which is also unknown. Or because of the illnesses of Puyi and Zhao Xinbo, they have suffered a major blow, and there are more and more infected people. This depends on the strength of the bodies of the traitors in general and how strong their resistance is to determine their condition.

On the River

— Zhou Han

I am so afraid of sitting on ocean-going ships that I almost lose my soul. Whenever I think of sitting on a ship, I get a headache. I have already told you that I am going to Hankou. On the day I sent the letter, I was troubled all night by the problem of sitting on a ship. I asked a friend if there was a way to get from Nanjing to Hankou without taking a ship. The friend told me that there was, to take a train from Pukou to Zhengzhou, and then transfer to the Jinghan Railway to reach Hankou. This was such joyous news to me. I decided not to take a ship and go by the Yangtze River waterway, but to take a train through Pukou. However, on the same day, I received a letter from my older brother saying that since you are going to Hankou for a trip, why not come to Jiujiang for a few days first? Moreover, my sister-in-law also added a few words, saying that we have been separated for many years and she really wants to meet me, and that I must first go to their place, Jiujiang. To go to Jiujiang first and then to Hankou, shouldn't I take the Yangtze River waterway? Isn't it impossible to take a train, but only to take a steamer? This really annoyed and angered me. It has really been many years since I have seen my older brother and sister-in-law. If I don't go and see them this time, how can I justify it? And my clever little niece, I also want to see her. If I take the train to Hankou and then go to Jiujiang to see them, it is possible, but from Hankou to Jiujiang is also the Yangtze River waterway. There is no train there, so isn't it the same? There was no way around it, so I had to muster up my courage and board a Yangtze River steamer. The Yangtze River steamer I took was a large China Merchants Bureau ship. Friends said that river ships and ocean-going ships are completely different, especially since this is a large ship. At first, I didn't believe it, so I went to sleep as soon as I got on board, preparing to get so dizzy that I couldn't get up. However, river ships are really not like ocean-going ships. There wasn't even a ripple. It was really as steady as Mount Tai. In this way, I looked at the scenery along the river every day, and I was so happy that I felt like a child again.

You remember the Han River in our hometown, right? Once, I took a small motorboat from Chenghai to Shantou. Although there were also many fields on both sides, the villages were all neat, with tall houses. How are the two sides of the Yangtze River? From Nanjing to Wuhu and Anqing, the houses on both sides are all mud and bamboo huts, and they are in groups of two or three, not forming villages. Looking into the distance, there are one or two villages, but the houses are only a few dozen. Where are the large villages with hundreds or thousands of houses and tall buildings on both sides of the Han River? From this point of view, the provinces in the Yangtze River basin are really not as good as the Han River basin.

I think the most beautiful scenery on the river is the evening glow. Have you seen it? At about five o'clock, the setting sun slants westward. At first, several golden rays of light radiate from the white clouds in the sky. Later, the fiery red sun appears on the azure mountains in the west, rolling down behind the mountains as if panting. In my eyes, the fiery red sun is round and large, so large that it looks like a bamboo tray used by silkworm farmers in the countryside. That proves that my eyes are not good. Some people say that if people with good eyesight look at it, it is not so big, but only a little bigger than the Mid-Autumn Festival moon. After the sun rolls down behind the mountains, the clouds in the sky are even more beautiful. That is the evening glow. The golden clouds change into peach-red, then into violet, and then gradually fade, and the curtain of night opens. When the clouds in the sky are putting on makeup, the waters of the river are also holding a makeup dance party. The waters of the Yangtze River are originally ephedra-colored. When the sunlight shines on them, they turn golden, and then they turn purple-red. The water flows and surges, they are so active and beautiful.

On the ship, although it is quieter than the train? There is no noise of the train's engine, nor is there any shaking of the train. However, you know, the noise of the passengers makes me unable to be quiet. They set up several mahjong tables in the hall to play cards. Except for meal times, they play from day to night, from night to dawn. The sound of talking, the sound of shouting, the sound of playing cards. Sometimes, a loud shout startles me awake from my dreams. It's really annoying. Jiujiang is almost here. I'll tell you later. In short, the river makes me unafraid. But it also makes me unable to have any peace.

Economic Burden

— Jie Hua

Tropical Bay

— Xi

I live not far from the sea. If you go up a small mountain south of my house, you can see a patch of deep blue water through the gaps in the distant trees. That patch of water sometimes shakes up, as high as the treetops; sometimes it shakes down, until it cannot be seen; that is the bay. The tropical bay is very beautiful, there is sound and color there. The sound is rhythmic, and the color is harmonious.

The coast is surrounded by coconut trees. The road is in the coconut grove. Walking in the coconut grove is such an interesting thing; the tide ebbs and flows, drawing near and receding, so clearly. The wind from the sea is always blowing that way. The high wind blows on the tops of the coconut trees, and the coconut leaves sway, turning over and over, harmonizing with the tide. The lower wind brushes the weeds, and the weeds brush my feet.

I walk from the coconut grove to the bay, and the more I go forward, the more and thicker the sand becomes, which increases my interest. The coconut grove is so quiet, without a trace of human breath. There is only the rhythm of nature; the tide and the sound of the wind. The sandy road is so white and winding, and few people walk there. There are many unknown birds in the forest, and their calls are so harmonious; most of them are magpies, very lively and free, flicking their long tails as they jump on the ground. They are not afraid of me, chasing each other in twos and threes so freely, seeming to be arrogant, not noticing that there is another part of the animal world.

As I walk, I gradually feel some wetness under my feet. In the footprints of my feet, there is already some water. It was dusk. The bay in the sunset is unforgettable to me. Everything is in a rhythmic sound wave, keeping silent, not disturbing each other. The ones that can move and can sing, naturally give them a share of happiness, making them sing, harmonize, and fly. Some birds, probably seagulls, chase the waves as if they were living things. In the foamy part of the waves, they stop their feet, and when that layer of foam disappears and becomes another layer of waves, they fly up again. The scene is so leisurely and lively. It is really too natural. Only in that place can a person truly show his humanity, loving all things, loving the waves, loving the foam, loving the sea claws, loving the wind, loving the leaves············Everything will harmonize with his heart, and everything will arouse his respect and love.

The seawater gradually turns golden yellow. I think that if I look at the bay from the distant mountains facing the sunset, it should be another kind of fun. The patch of gold that can be seen through the gaps in the trees should be more lively, more vast, and more difficult to grasp. It is peaceful, and perhaps you can still see smoke and mist on the water. Smoke and mist will spread, covering the scene with a blur. That is very intoxicating.

There are no large ships in the bay, only a few fishing boats. They all drift back from the direction of the sunset. The sunset waits for them, and the sea breeze sends them off. Seagulls lead the way for them, and the tops of the coconut trees gather their songs:

Not afraid of the sea, not afraid of the waves, rowing the oars more. Pushing the punting pole more, rowing, rowing, rowing over the higher tide··············

So they row again, and the small boat rises and falls in their songs. The fatigue of the day may be eliminated in that tone. "Gua·········Gua," the seagulls harmonize with them. Then there is a burst of laughter, several loud conversations between neighboring boats, and then there are the waves again. Again, the wind. All of these have the sunset waiting on the beach.

As soon as the sunset sinks, the tide becomes angry.

The sunset at sea is also very beautiful, the entire sea of golden yellow, gradually receding. Finally, there is only a ray of light left on the sea; it is leaping. The end of the light is turbid yellow. Turbid yellow is gradually swallowed by the sunset glow. Then, the haze attacks, and the haze thickens layer by layer, turning into night. The night in the bay is vast.

In the night, only the sea water surges against the stars. There is no clear light on the sea, and the fishing boats are all tied to the coconut trees. I want to see the fishing lights rising and falling with the waves, but I can't see them. Only the sea water is surging, surging, like the original sea, without a trace of human breath.

I found a shop in the bay and stayed there overnight, listening to the tide all night. When the morning sun sprinkled another kind of brilliance on the sea, I said goodbye to the bay. I did not see the sea's morning makeup, I regret it very much. On my way back, I only thought of the seagulls flying so slowly.

Xiao Xiao's Art of Living

— Bing

Jane Austen once said:

"What is the purpose of living in this world? Isn't it just to laugh at others sometimes, and be laughed at by others sometimes?"

This is the ultimate art of living. There are many discussions about the art of living in the world, but none are as unique and interesting as these two sentences. Living in this world is indeed just like this—and must be like this—to spend one's life smoothly. Since ancient times, how many people have taken life too seriously, resulting in being disliked everywhere, and ending up depressed. Some even fail to protect their heads and die unnaturally, all because they did not understand the original meaning of this art of living with a smile. Conversely, those who know how to laugh, even if they do not achieve rapid promotion, will always have no enemies in the world. Everyone says he is a good

Page 23

In this way, their lifespan will always be higher than that of ordinary people. When they die, they still have a smiling face, and after their death, everyone cries out in unison, saying: "Alas, the world has lost a good gentleman!"

In today's world, the dangers of society are known to everyone. Therefore, this art of living with a smile is even more needed and more widespread. The strong men running on the political stage, who take laughter as a practical raft for living in the world, can mostly "do whatever they want". Many things that cannot be resolved are often resolved satisfactorily in laughter. Seeing that it is about to explode, they will definitely hold the "safely passed" ticket. The explosion of Yi Peiji's theft and sale of antiques is said to be mainly because his face was too rigid and he did not know how to laugh, offending many people. Moreover, those who know how to laugh not only can turn around in all aspects, but also have nothing to fear when the political stage encounters a change.

And so on. Those who mingle in small venues, such as ordinary institutions, companies, and schools, are also in the world of people who know how to laugh. No, in these small places, the art of living with a smile is even more popular and more effective.

To go one step further, even if you have old rice to eat at home, you must know the art of laughing. Didn't the ancients say? If you don't know how to laugh, "won't disaster come from the sky?" It is always good to be able to laugh between family members. Especially those who have a house full of wives and concubines must learn this trick.

Dear readers, do you know how to laugh? Living in this kind of society, you really deserve to die if you don't hurry up and learn this trick.

Fireside Chat

— Wu Pumin

Snow fell, and the stove in the room was lit early. The warmth in the room felt like spring.

People living in spring are intoxicated. But the snow is fluttering outside the window! It is the season of severe winter! However, people lying quietly by the fireside reading their favorite poetry collections are also intoxicated.

Occasionally, while reading a poem about snow, I happened to look up and see the snow falling outside the window. A sudden urge to watch the snow arose spontaneously. I put the poetry collection aside, stood up, walked to the window, and unfolded the white gauze curtain with woven flowers. Gazing at the snowy scene on the road outside, I couldn't help but feel deeply disappointed. Because it wasn't as beautiful as described in the poem, nor was it a vast expanse of white. As soon as it landed on the ground, it was ruined, turning into black, dirty water, splashing on the hems of people's clothes and being carried home.

However, as soon as I opened the window, a sharp gust of cold wind rolled into the room, and I quickly closed it.

"What cold weather!" I confessed to myself.

Suddenly, I looked down and saw the pedestrians on the road, all wearing short clothes, as if blood was boiling in their veins. They walked fearlessly through the snow on the road, their heroic spirit truly that of brave warriors!

"How cowardly I am!" I thought, "Why did I close the window after only a gust of cold wind? Why do I have to hide by this spring-like fireside?"

When I sat by the fireside again and opened the poetry collection, two lines of poetry from my friend Mr. Zhou suddenly fell out: "Not a follower of fleeting favor, without a stove, how long can one endure the cold?"

I felt a sudden surge of shame and lowered my head to my chest. But this was somewhat like being intoxicated in spring! ·············

Sinology

Ms. Wang Shuimei's Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Staying at Wang Changling's Hermitage by Chang Jian

Clear streams unfathomable, a lonely cloud in seclusion, sunlight peeks through the pines, its clear light still for you. A thatched pavilion rests in the shadow of flowers, a medicine garden nourishes mossy patterns. I too shall bid farewell to worldly affairs, and join the cranes in the Western Mountains. Climbing with Gao Shi and Xue Ju, the Cien Temple Pagoda, Cen Shen's tower seems to surge forth, solitary and towering to the sky. Ascending the palace, reaching beyond the world, the stone steps wind through the void. Towering over Shenzhou, rugged as a ghost's work, its four corners obstruct the white sun, its seven stories brush the azure sky. Looking down, one points to high-flying birds, listening, one hears the startled wind. The continuous mountains are like waves, rushing together like the eastward tide, green locust trees line the road, palaces and mansions are exquisitely adorned. Autumn colors come from the west, filling the passes with a somber hue. On the northern plains of the Five Mausoleums, ancient and misty green, pure reason can be understood, a superior cause is our long-held principle. I vow to hang up my official hat, and seek endless enlightenment.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Katharine Hepburn's Transformation

— Shu Min

It is said that she has changed her arrogant and obstinate temper.

And has realized the importance of publicity.

Katharine Hepburn's temper has changed, can you believe it? Her temper is strange and obstinate. If you say that she has changed her temper now, few people would believe it. Westerners say that the spots on a leopard will not change, and Chinese people also say that it is easy to change the landscape but difficult to alter one's nature. Now saying that Katharine's nature has changed, isn't that saying that the spots on a leopard can also move?

But this wildcat-like Katharine Hepburn, it is said that her temper has really changed.

They say that this is not a matter of one day or two, but a gradual shift between the filming of "Little Women" and the filming of "A Little Minister". It is said that the reasons are very complex. Perhaps it was due to emotional stimulation after the divorce. Perhaps it was due to the advice of her manager, Leland Hayward. But the biggest reason is probably the failure she suffered when she performed on stage in New York. In any case, this proud, obstinate, stubborn Katharine Hepburn has indeed had a turn for the better.

A few months ago, the publicity department of Aihua Company would get a headache whenever they heard Katharine Hepburn's name mentioned. Her every move was enough to hinder their work and make them feel embarrassed, turning their achievements to ashes. Her arrogance and rudeness towards reporters had long placed her in a position of being unpopular with the public. She herself thought that as long as her performance was outstanding, everything else could be ignored. Now the situation is different. The publicity department of the company has changed its attitude towards Katharine Hepburn, and now values and praises her. What they are most pleased about is that she is doing her best to cooperate with the company's publicity work. She has realized the importance of publicity value. This is a lesson she has learned from experience. She has read countless articles attacking her in newspapers and magazines. She has heard countless sarcastic and abusive remarks from film critics. Especially important, the harsh criticism she received when she performed on stage in New York forced her to admit the authority of reporters and drama and film critics, as well as the value of publicity work, and made her turn back.

Of course, this lesson is a cruel one, and her transformation is also a painful and unwilling one. It can be said that she turned back only after hitting her head full of bumps. Fortunately, she realized it early enough, and did not reach the point of being beyond redemption.

An important part of the publicity department's work is taking still photos. That is, the still photos taken after each day's filming, specifically for publicity in newspapers. Katharine used to be very unwilling to take these still photos. The company's publicity department was also most afraid of mentioning this matter to her, but they had to ask her to take them. Now the situation is different. Katharine is very willing to take still photos herself, often sitting for several hours without showing any fatigue. If the negative is not good, she tears it up herself, saying that she will reshoot it the next day. Isn't this attitude completely different from before?

Even her attitude towards colleagues and supporting actors is different from before. When she was filming commercials (that is, short films for advertising), she once said to the director: "Why don't you put the other actresses in first, and then add my part?" Promoting others instead of herself in "A Little Minister" is not only not something Katharine Hepburn would have done in the past, but also something that previous stars would not have been willing to do.

There was another time when she was filming a short advertisement, she insisted on inviting John Beal to film with her. She said that he was the "little minister" in "A Little Minister" and should be given some glory. This selfless heart and the all-out cooperation with the publicity department are truly commendable. According to the announcement by the authorities of Aihua Company, this wildcat-like Katharine Hepburn has indeed changed into a new person.

But whether a person's nature can be changed is still a question. A person's nature is certainly not like the spots on a leopard, which will not change at all, but the change of human nature may be a temporary change under stimulation, and will gradually change back. Furthermore, this may be the company's publicity to ease the negative feelings of reporters towards Katharine. Let us wait and see what happens.

Review of "College Rhythm"

— Ji Han

STudenTour Nanjing

In Hollywood, treating movies as a game did not start today. At the same time, this playful attitude is related to the decline of European and American films as a whole. Furthermore, films like "College Rhythm" are not overly emphasizing business considerations, and therefore obviously take a joking attitude, bringing together events that easily excite or intoxicate people, and using them as the main expressions. For example, boat racing, song and dance, and students' romances are taken as themes that can sell tickets.

However, on the contrary, these events put together result in vulgarity and emptiness. In fact, it organizes an imaginary story, just joking around. What is even more regrettable is that it did not achieve the success that the authors expected. For example, the boat racing scene is not tense enough, the progress of the story is very chaotic, and the dance scenes are not enough to express the splendor of capitalist films. Among them, only a few love songs, although they are so-called decadent tunes, can gain good feelings among the audience.

We don't have excessive demands on American movies, and we have seen a lot of joking movies, but like this "College Rhythm", it is indeed not worthy of praise. When we can't find any merit in it except for hearing a few loud songs, then...

Review of "Resistance"

— You Jing

"Sniper" 丨丨丨 Carlton

After a series of old, mediocre, empty, shallow, and boring films depicting assassination, jealousy, vinegar-drinking, suicide, and aimless uproar that made people feel extremely bored and weary, watching this "Resistance" film could not help but evoke a sense of excitement!

This is not only because "Resistance" is a war film with intense, fierce, tense, and terrifying emotions, and a tone of explosions, assaults, misery, and tragedy, but also because it shows us a more realistic page in the midst of real-world turmoil. There is no exaggeration, nor has anything been concealed.

The story unfolds fifteen years ago. Groups of women throw flowers to celebrate the neatly marching troops. It concludes with countless white bones and snow-white crosses as the prologue to the film. Next, it depicts the stalemate between the Allied British and French forces and the German army on the "silent Western Front," where five or six hundred people are shot down by enemy snipers every day. In the helplessness of not being able to detect the enemy snipers' location and wasting bullets on shooting, two Russian youths, Slidin and Siberiski, known as sharpshooters, are transferred from the shooting reconnaissance training school in the rear to serve. They discover the enemy's secret on an evening of storms and terror, kill the opposing sniper, and drag the body back. Afterwards, the Allied forces launch a major offensive and seize much land.

At this time, changes occur within Russia. With the dissemination of revolutionary news in the "Pravda" newspaper, the majority of Russian soldiers leave the Allied trenches and return to their country. The two sharpshooters also take different paths due to their differing understandings of the war.

Siberiski, who returns home, works in a border railway repair factory, constantly training young male and female workers in his shooting skills. In a foreign invasion, Siberiski uses his excellent shooting skills to fulfill his duty of defense, and the last person he shoots is his former classmate and friend, Slidin.

From a screenwriting perspective, this script cannot be considered entirely perfect, and the performance also uses many methods used in other war films. However, its exceptional quality lies in its truthful and moving depiction of two different wars.

Several points are worth mentioning, such as the depiction of the lives between officers and soldiers: on one side, gramophone records, beer, singing, and the longing for women; on the other side, struggling on the line of death. Also, the decline and growth of the two individuals in the era are depicted concisely and profoundly through their origins and essence. Finally, the overly optimistic "no resistance" theory of the playing basketball youth and the verification of Siberiski's argument, etc., are also analyzed and contrasted in relation to reality.

Collection of Brief Comments

— Lin Qin

(1)

Ruan Lingyu's marital discord has been widely reported by various newspapers, indicating that the lives of female celebrities have garnered significant attention in the eyes of the general public.

(2)

New talents Diao Banhua, Mei Lin, and Xu Wen have now been noticed by Lianhua as potential leading actresses.

(3)

Wei Wei says he is preparing a small projector to publicly screen "The Light of Children" in rural areas, absolutely free of charge, to express their intention to promote education. Who would do something that doesn't earn a penny? Only them!

(4)

Fatty Yin said: "God! Art! Bread! Big Cakes!"

"Lakeside Songs and Dances" – Full of Laughter and Excitement

— Yunmen

This is a grand comedy from MGM, introducing the latest and most innovative songs and dances of 1935. The entire play mainly depicts the lives of young people on campus. Most comedies inevitably resort to those boring farces or shallow jokes. However, "Lakeside Songs and Dances" is constructed based on modern trends and the symbolism of youth. We know that the symbolism of modern youth is the extremely lively pursuit of progress and enjoyment. Indeed, books as stiff as mummies cannot restrain the vigorous new life. Old concepts and outdated ideas that taste like chewing wax and erode the soul can never shackle our 20th-century minds. Those gentlemenly manners that prohibit impropriety should be allowed to adapt to the times and be used as poses on the battlefield. Those rigid moral principles should be allowed to decay into fossils. Therefore, young people must live vibrantly, walk the path of life, and nakedly pursue what they love. This is the symbolism given by the "Sea University" during its campus tour.

In addition to the old comedy duo Laurel and Hardy, there is a new pair of counterparts. They are the big-nosed rambling Dr. Jimmy Durante and the seemingly well-meaning Mr. Jills White. At the same time, there are twenty all-American standard beauties, all of whom are the most beautiful campus belles from various universities in the United States. Now that "Lakeside Songs and Dances" has been filmed, it can also be called a "Campus Beauty Pageant." The various song and dance performances are truly worthy of being the latest style of 1935 and will be popular all over the world. Moreover, the beauty of the world's great nature is also used as a backdrop. The most innovative and outstanding songs are "New Moon," "Carol," "Snake Dance," "Struggle," "Taj Mahal," "University Song," and "The Future is Long." The final scene of rowing races is even more lively and exciting. Therefore, "Lakeside Songs and Dances" is not only a must-see for students but also an excellent piece of art for those who love beautiful arts and songs and dances, offering a refreshing experience.

Submission Guidelines for the Shenbao Film Supplement

This publication is a film publication that assists in cultural promotion and art. It welcomes external contributions. Once published, generous compensation will be provided.

Once the text is published and compensated, the copyright belongs to Shenbao.

The text in this publication is mainly in vernacular Chinese and must use modern punctuation.

Each submission must be stamped; otherwise, it will not be compensated.

Due to limited space in this publication, the text should be as concise as possible. Each submission should be limited to around 500 words.

If the submission is a translation, the original work should be attached. Avoid mixing in English if possible.

Unless otherwise stated in advance and return postage is included, this publication is not responsible for preserving or returning manuscripts, photos, etc.

Do not write on both sides of the paper, write horizontally, or use a pencil.

Submissions that are duplicated, copied, or directly transcribed explanations will not be compensated upon detection.

Film Novel

Waiting to Marry (Forsaking All Others) (8)

— Su Yin

Before Marilyn could call him to stop, it was too late. Durrant's pillow flew over with a whoosh, hitting the kerosene lamp squarely. The kerosene lamp overturned and immediately caught fire. A scarf hanging on the piano also caught fire. Durrant and Marilyn rushed over to put out the fire. Unexpectedly, in the chaos, the woman's underwear Durrant was wearing caught fire in the back. By the time Marilyn frantically put out the fire for him, a large area of Durrant's back had already been burned. Of course, from then on, Durrant moaned all night and no longer talked about love.

The next morning, Geoffrey and Paula arrived. Since last night, Paula had been worried because Marilyn hadn't come home late, so she ran to Geoffrey to ask for help in finding her. Geoffrey initially refused completely. Since Marilyn was so unconcerned about her own reputation, why should he worry about her? Moreover, since their decisive separation a few days ago, he didn't want to interfere in her affairs anymore. But then he thought again. Connie must be looking for Durrant now too. If she found them together, she would definitely make things difficult for Marilyn and not let her go. Geoffrey's old feelings for Marilyn eventually overcame his reason, and he agreed to go with Paula to find her. Geoffrey and Paula found the place. Geoffrey saw that the door to the house was locked and there was no sound inside. He couldn't help but feel jealous and said, "What a gentle nest!" Paula looked at him but didn't say anything. After waiting for a while, she said, "I have the key here. But we need to decide, before we go in, should we ring the doorbell or knock?" Geoffrey snorted and said, "When you encounter this kind of thing, the usual method is to split the door open with an axe." Paula said nothing, opened the door with the key, and the two of them went in together.

When they went in, Marilyn was just coming downstairs, her clothes all fixed. She was holding Durrant's clothes, intending to deliver them to him. She suddenly saw the two of them come in and couldn't help but stand there in a daze. Paula shouted, "Marilyn, darling, are you okay?" Marilyn said, "Of course I'm okay, what are you doing here? How did you know..." Paula said, "Mrs. Leiter... the woman who gave you the key... she made a phone call... she said it was really a strange thing. Of course, I told her it was okay... but, Marilyn, what is this about?" Marilyn angrily said, "Why do you listen to those gossiping women?" After she finished speaking, she walked towards the living room to deliver the clothes to Durrant.

As she walked past Geoffrey, she felt a little embarrassed and ignored him, walking straight past. Geoffrey couldn't help but say, "This isn't where I should be. I didn't want to come in the first place." Marilyn stubbornly said, "Since you didn't want to come, why did you come?" Geoffrey said, "I came because I needed to. You seem to have forgotten. Durrant is a married man, and if his wife finds out, she will publicize your affair in newspapers all over the country." Marilyn defiantly said, "Let her publicize it then. She lost her husband, so maybe that can give her some comfort." Geoffrey said, "What, she lost her husband?" Marilyn deliberately said, "Yes, that's right." Geoffrey grunted. Marilyn shouted, "What does it matter? Please tell me. I have my freedom, I'm white, and I'm over twenty-one!" Geoffrey also shouted, "And a fool! Who deserves a spanking."

Paula interjected, "Don't yell... um, who's going to take the clothes to Durrant?" Marilyn saw this and handed Durrant's clothes to Geoffrey, saying, "He's sleeping in the guest room. You take them to him." Geoffrey walked into the guest room. Durrant was sleeping on his back, half of the blanket had fallen to the floor, revealing the burned area on his back. Geoffrey saw this and couldn't help but feel pleased. He walked forward and pushed him. Durrant cried out and opened his eyes. Seeing Geoffrey, he shouted, "Old friend, old friend. Did you bring the doctor?" Geoffrey asked, "What doctor? What's wrong?" (To be continued)
